Silver Bill Unlikely to Pass US Congress; Roosevelt Decides to Delay Policy; Senate Silver Faction Negotiates with President 50

(Washington) According to well-informed political observers, there is little hope for the passage of the Silver Bill in this session of Congress. Although the White House has issued a statement by President Roosevelt requesting Congress to express its attitude on monetary issues, observers now believe that President Roosevelt has asked the leaders of both houses to shelve the Silver Bill and other currency bills in this session of Congress. It is said that President Roosevelt has now notified the leaders of the House that he will use the powers conferred by the Thomas Amendment to expand the utility of silver. This statement was also confirmed by Lanay when he met with the Associated Press reporter this afternoon. According to Lanay, there is sufficient indication that the Silver Bill will not be passed in this session because this session is scheduled to close in mid-May. President Roosevelt will use the powers conferred by the Thomas Amendment to support silver. Lanay continued that the President's opposition to the passage of the silver bill in this session is very obvious because the President wants to allow the silver purchase program to demonstrate what achievements it can ultimately have. However, the President strongly supports the Dies Bill, so he may not veto the bill. The silver faction in Congress met today and decided to directly petition President Roosevelt to cancel his plan to shelve the silver bill. Democratic Senator King hopes to have a consultation with the President within two or three days. At the same time, the various silver factions have decided to focus on the Dies Bill and hope that it will become the only silver bill passed by Congress. (National Telegram, 16th)

Case of Secret Importation of a Large Quantity of Firearms from Japan (Japanese Correspondence) - Over 30,000 Pistols, 330,000 Rounds of Ammunition 85

The meticulousness and rigor of the Japanese police are renowned as second in the world. Almost no illegal behavior can escape the reach of the law. However, in recent years, the underground movements of leftist groups have become particularly developed. Repeated investigations have failed to extinguish the intense movement, and it has even shown signs of spreading like wildfire. The right-wing movement can also gain the sympathy of some people and even receive assistance from active-duty soldiers and veterans, thus making their actions more convenient. However, their weakness lies in the lack of weapons. Pistols and bullets can be bought and sold openly in Japan, but not as freely as in European and American countries. They must be restricted by local police officials. For example, if someone wants to buy a pistol and some bullets, they must register with the police station. They must also report the use of each bullet. Otherwise, if a suicide or homicide case occurs, the person with the pistol should be inspected. However, under such a dense organization, the number of unregistered guns in Japanese society is countless, and this does not include the guns carried by the army and navy. Therefore, assassination cases continue to occur. High-ranking officials, whether *zaibatsu* or bureaucrats, are always vigilant and dare not say that nothing will happen.

This large-scale secret importation of pistols was discovered when the authorities investigated the robbery at the Kawasaki Hundredth Bank branch in Omori. The Communist Party's firearms were supplied by the Koda Firearms and Gunpowder Store in Kobe. At that time, Koda To was arrested and sentenced to one year in prison by the Osaka District Court. He refused to accept the sentence and appealed. He was released on bail in February of last year. However, he still refused to give up his secret business. In the warehouses of other accomplices, he still had 3,804 pistols and 333,800 rounds of ammunition. This is only what has been discovered. It is not known how much remains undiscovered. Because they operate very skillfully, their organization is very precise, and the people involved are very extensive, it is still impossible to be certain whether the number discovered is accurate. Now, let's give a brief account of Koda To himself.

Koda To is the main figure in this large-scale secret importation of pistols. His ancestral home is in Morioka Prefecture. He studied at Morioka Commercial School. At the age of fourteen, he dropped out of school and operated a gunpowder shop in Kobe with his uncle, Horio Eisuke. He lost five fingers on his right hand in an gunpowder explosion. He lived in that gunpowder shop for eight years, and thus understood the management methods of guns, cannons, and gunpowder. In Taisho 13 (1924), he obtained a license to operate a guns, cannons, and gunpowder shop himself. He then opened the Koda Firearms and Gunpowder Store in Kanomachi, Kobe. At that time, after the European War, there were many German small pistols left over from the war and overproduction, and there were no sales channels. Koda saw the way to come, and used his own years of training and the licensed gunpowder shop to contact the authorities to implement the large-scale import of pistols and the distribution of other military equipment. Therefore, he also obtained a license for a non-military goods repair shop. At that time, he resold the guns, cannons, and bullets imported from Germany to Tianjin, Qingdao, Manchuria, and other places. As a result, he made huge profits, owning assets of over a million. He then used mail ships traveling to and from Europe, only bringing back some parts of firearms, and then assembling them upon his return. The Japanese authorities also used this kind of business to sell guns to China, which was tolerable and beneficial to its aggression.

However, the only purpose of this profit-seeking business is to make profit. The so-called patriotic words are only a superficial saying. When there is great profit to be made, he will sacrifice his patriotism. Therefore, the Communist Party's weapons can be secretly purchased from the Koda Firearms and Gunpowder Store, and the same goes for right-wing groups. The selling price is 92 Japanese yen per Browning pistol and 45 yen for a revolver. At least 30,000 or more of these have been sold secretly in Japan, with no less than 400,000 rounds of ammunition. This will naturally

further arouse unease in Japanese society and shake the order of the political world. Only then did they begin searching and detain Koda. However, the firearms have already been dispersed. What has now been found is only what is stored in the warehouses, and the real difficulty does not lie in these few hundred seized guns. (April 13th, Tokyo)

Japan Controls Coal Mines in Northeast China - Establishes Manchurian Coal Mine Company with Capital of 16 Million Yuan 86

Liaoning Correspondence: Japan is actively developing the rich mineral resources of Northeast China, nominally in the name of joint ventures between Japan and the puppet regime, and ordering the puppet state to contribute a portion of the funds. In reality, however, the power is entirely in the hands of the Japanese, completely controlled by the Japanese side. Recently, the so-called Japanese-puppet joint venture Manchurian Coal Mine Joint Stock Company was established, with a capital of 16 million yuan (of which 6.8 million yuan is invested by the puppet state's industrial sector, 1.2 million yuan is invested by the puppet Central Bank, 5 million yuan is invested by the South Manchuria Railway's industries, and 3 million yuan is in cash). In addition to the coal mines already mined by the South Manchuria Railway in Yantai and Benxihu, there are still large amounts of buried coal, all of which are controlled and developed by the coal mine company. The following is a summary of each coal mine:

Fuzhou Coal Mine 87

The coal mine in Wuhuzui, Fuxian County, is extremely famous, about nineteen kilometers from Wafangdian Station, about eight kilometers from Sanlibao Station, and about forty minutes by sea from Sandawan. This coal mine was discovered during the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty. It was first operated by Chinese using native methods, and later fell into the hands of the Russians. After the Russo-Japanese War, the coal mine began to have relations with Japan, but it was still operated by Yan Wengui, a Chinese merchant from Dalian. Because of his strong capital, the business was very good. After Zhou's death, the coal mine was placed under the jurisdiction of the Northeast Mining Bureau of the former Liaoning Province. After the September 18th Incident broke out, the Mining Bureau was dissolved and taken over by the puppet state, which entrusted the South Manchuria Railway to operate it. The amount of coal buried in the coal mine has not been fully measured, so there are no accurate statistics, but according to the investigation of the old Northeast Mining Bureau, it is about 16 million tons. The coal mine has thirteen layers, with an average thickness of one meter to three meters. Because the coal is loose and weak, there are very few large pieces of coal, but because it has a semi-metallic luster, it can become anthracite coal, and the sulfur content is relatively low, so it is quite suitable for use as a raw material for coking. The coal mine's output is about 200,000 tons per year, based on past performance. Its sales channels are the three northeastern provinces, South China, Shandong, and various places in mainland Japan. The coal mine is the only place to supply anthracite coal in Manchuria and is close to the seaport, so its future is promising due to these superior conditions.

Badaoju Coal Mine 88

Badaoju Station in Heishan County, Liaoning Province, is about one kilometer south of the Datong Line, about three kilometers from Dahushan, about 137 kilometers from Jinzhou, and about 160 kilometers from Fengtian. It was discovered by local people in the eighth year of the Republic of China, and they began small-scale mining. Later, when Zhang Zuolin was the Inspector General, he inspected the area and paid attention to the coal mine. He sent his chief of staff to manage it, mainly to supply military needs. During the September 18th Incident, because it was managed by the Northeast Mining Bureau, it was confiscated and is now entrusted to the South Manchuria Railway for continued operation. Although the exact amount of coal buried in the coal mine has not yet been determined, it is estimated to be around 20 million tons. There are five or six coal seams, with a thickness of about one meter to five meters. The coal is mostly bituminous coal, with some close to lignite. Because it is jet black, it has a fatty luster, but this kind of coal is very easy to weather, so it is difficult to have any hope. The coal's sales channels are mainly Fengtian, Jinzhou, Yingkou, Tongliao, and along the Datong Line, for use in power plants. However, because there is no large market nearby, and it is hit by Fushun coal and Beipiao coal, it is increasingly in a difficult situation. However, the Japanese are planning to revive it.

Weiming Mountain Coal Mine 89

Weiming Mountain is in Liaoyang County, Liaoning Province, about seven or eight kilometers south of the Yantai Coal Mine, which belongs to the South Manchuria Railway, about 43 kilometers to Liaoyang, and about 71 kilometers to Shenyang. Although there was a fact that Koreans mined the coal mine in the early days, it was operated by the Tianhe Company, a Sino-Russian joint venture, in the 28th year of the Guangxu reign. After the Russo-Japanese War, the Russian rights were lost. In the third year of the Republic of China, the Liaoning Provincial Department of Finance invested in it, and it became a self-operated business of the provincial government. After the September 18th Incident, although it was temporarily managed by the local public security maintenance association, the mining was stopped due to the activities of the militia. Although there are no accurate statistics on the amount of coal buried in the coal mine, there are about 1.7 million tons in the Weiming area and about 7.68 million tons in the Xintai Peninsula area, totaling about 9 million tons. The coal mine is part of the Yantai Coal Mine. There are a total of eighteen coal seams, but only five have been mined, with a thickness of one meter to two meters. Due to the various differences in the coal seams, there are both anthracite and bituminous coal. As for sales channels, it has only been sold in Shenyang, Liaoyang, Yingkou, and other places, mostly for use in coal stoves. During the era of cheap silver, there was a considerable revival, but it is now at a disadvantage due to competition with Yantai coal.

Xinqiu Coal Mine 90

Xinqiu is in Fuxin County, Rehe Province, in the mining areas of the Daxin and Daxing companies. It is 32 kilometers from Xinlitun Station on the Datong Line to the mining area. The coal mine was discovered in the 30th year of the Guangxu reign. It was first operated by the Beijing-Fengtian Railway. In the third year of the Republic of China, a technician from the Japanese Okura Group went to the area to inspect it, but was killed on the way, and demanded compensation, and then acquired the rights to the mining area. The Daxin and Daxing companies were reorganized as Sino-Japanese joint ventures. Before the September 18th Incident, the coal mine was exclusively needed by some parts of the testing cones. After the incident, mining was stopped due to the unrest. The amount of coal buried in the coal mine has not been thoroughly investigated, so its exact number is unknown, but according to the general measurement, the number should be 1.1 billion tons. The coal mine's coal seams are, from a general perspective, about three layers, with the lowest part being the best, and its thickness is particularly high, averaging from six meters to ten meters. Although the coal is very good, part of it is mostly bituminous coal that is jet black and very intolerant of fire, and is quite similar to Fushun coal. The coal's sales channels are only in the vicinity of the coal mine and Fuxin, Xinlitun, Heishan, Yixian, and other places, with a very small scope. However, the amount of coal buried in the coal mine is very rich in Manchuria, and it is also relatively easy to mine, so after the completion of the Huludao Seaport, the coal area can be used as the second Fushun.

Heligang Coal Mine 91

Heligang is in Yangyuan County, Heilongjiang Province, about 500 kilometers down the Songhua River from Harbin, on the opposite bank of Jiamusi. There are more than 50 kilometers of railway dedicated to coal mines from Yunjiang, which can directly reach the mining area. The coal mine was discovered in the third year of the Republic of China. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, it began to be mined through official-merchant joint ventures. Zhang Xueliang, Wu Junsheng, and Guangxin Company all had very large relations with it. However, the local authorities, feeling the difficulty of funding, even had the idea of selling it to foreigners for a time. After the September 18th Incident, with the mediation of the puppet state's Ministry of Industry, a company was organized this spring to continue mining. The amount of coal buried in the coal mine is about 300 million tons in the old area and 300 million tons in the planned new mining area, totaling 600 million tons. There are six coal seams in the old mining area, with the thickest coal seam being four meters. There are also six coal seams in the new mining area, with a thickness of seven meters to ten meters. There are four open-pit mining areas, with a total area of 41,000 square meters and a depth of 15 meters. From the mountain peaks to the banks of the Songhua River, there are coal transportation railways for transportation, so its sales channels are along the Songhua River and the fuel for ships sailing on the river, as well as the Northern Manchurian, Hu-Hai, and Qi-Ke Railways, which are often its customers. Harbin, Anda, Suihua, Hailin, and other places are its main markets. The coal is a viscous, jet-black, high-quality bituminous coal, and its burial volume is particularly abundant. Even from the perspective of open-pit mining, it is beyond the reach of other coal areas. However, the Songhua River, which is its only transportation route, experiences obstacles in transportation when it freezes every winter, which is its shortcoming. Now, the Japanese are rushing to complete the railway network in order to increase the coal mine's output. (Northeast News Agency)

The Living Buddha Nor-na Hutuktu of Xikang Arrives in Guangzhou to Perform a Seven-Day Dharma Ceremony for Eliminating Disasters and Benefiting the People 92

Guangzhou Correspondence: Nor-na Hutuktu, a member of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and a Living Buddha from Xikang, arrived in Guangzhou on the 8th of this month with seven people, including Li Gonglie, Yongzhong Lama, Cao Yabo, Qian Wenzhu, Wang Weibai, Gu Yaoshan, and Wang Zicai. They first went to the Liurong Temple. Several thousand Buddhist followers in the province held a meeting to welcome them at the temple. In the afternoon, the Disaster Elimination and People's Benefit Dharma Assembly also held a welcome meeting at the Provincial People's Education Center, with even more devout men and women attending. Nor-na said to the crowd, "Since the establishment of the Republic of China, the five races have been one family. I came to Beijing in the 18th year of the Republic of China and performed Dharma ceremonies for society four times before and after. This time coming south is the fifth Dharma ceremony. I will sincerely pray to relieve suffering and help those in need. Both Confucianism and Buddhism advise people to do good. Evil comes from an evil heart, and good comes from a good heart. If people can practice Dr. Sun Yat-sen's so-called psychological transformation, the world will naturally be peaceful." After the meeting, Nor-na took a car to the Bailingshan Leili, ascended to Nengren Temple, and prepared for the Dharma ceremony. Later, because those seeking an audience came in droves and the altar had not yet been fully arranged, he went down the mountain on the 11th at the invitation of Chen Jitang to preach. The reporter took the opportunity to visit him at the temple. Nor-na said that this time the Dharma ceremony for the Disaster Elimination and People's Benefit Association would begin around the 13th and would take about seven days. Afterwards, he would grant initiations and establish karmic connections for his disciples at the request of the public. He plans to leave Guangzhou next month, not returning to Ningbo, and will return to Xikang via Annam or Yunnan Province. In the Kang-Tibetan region, all religions worship the Buddha. Although there is the Yellow Sect, the White Sect, and the Red Sect, there is actually no difference in doctrine. However, the Red Sect has the oldest history. The White Sect began in the 1903rd year of the true transmission of Sakyamuni, and the Yellow Sect has only been practiced in Kang-Tibet for more than 400 years. The Red Sect is divided into outer, inner, and innermost esoteric sects. Outer and inner esoteric sects are mostly worshiped in the front and rear Tibet, while in Xikang, outer, inner, and innermost esoteric sects are all worshiped. Esoteric and exoteric practices are both emphasized and interconnected. One cannot become a Buddha without the other. The government and religion of the Kang-Tibetan region have always been unified. There are four Hutuktus in Kang-Tibet who are in charge of religious, political, military, and other affairs. Tibet was formerly under the Panchen Lama, and later under the Dalai Lama. However, in Xikang, all religious, political, and military affairs are under my control. The population of Xikang is about 7 million. Because the area belongs to the border region, it has long been coveted by foreigners. A portion of Tibet has long been occupied by the British, and another portion has been invaded by the French. Recently, border wars have broken out again, and the future seems worrying.

(12th)

The Auditing Office Actively Rectifies the Changlu Salt Affairs, Appointing Zeng Yangfeng as Manager and Transport Commissioner 93

The Changlu salt affairs have long been known for their corruption and mismanagement. In particular, the anti-smuggling police are extremely corrupt, engaging in embezzlement and dereliction of duty. These malpractices have become deeply ingrained habits. They openly smuggle salt and extort fees, treating it as normal. They even fabricate charges and demand payments that are more than fifteen times the price of the salt. As a result, private smuggling has become rampant, and official sales have sharply decreased. In the twelfth year of the Republic [1923], the official sales in the Zheng'an area of the region were about 3.75 million dan [unit of dry measure]. Later, this number gradually decreased. By the twenty-second year of the Republic [1933], official sales were only about 2.64 million dan. The loss in tax revenue was about 8 million yuan. Ineffective anti-smuggling efforts were the main reason for this situation. The Chief Auditing Office, recognizing this problem, specifically appointed Chief Inspector Zeng Yangfeng to concurrently serve as Manager of the Changlu Branch Office and Transport Commissioner to carry out rectification. Since taking office, he has shown great determination to reform the system, and his achievements are already apparent. Both internal and external personnel have shown renewed vigor. In the past, it took a week after reporting the shipment to receive the approval documents and transportation permits. Now, they can be obtained the next day. Everything is no longer as slow and inefficient as it was before, and the bad practices have been eliminated. It is reported that the anti-smuggling team was reorganized into a tax police force on April 1st, with a total of 2,100 officers and police. They are divided into seven districts. The district chiefs are either selected from those who have rich experience in anti-smuggling in the district or transferred from the successful tax police officers of Lianghuai. A tax police soldier training institute has also been established. Officers and police are rotated for training to get to the root of the problem and make rectification easier. The Henan Inspection Bureau, which was previously funded by anti-smuggling donations, has been abolished. Its duties have been transferred to the Sales Supervision Bureau. The savings from this have been used to train three special task force squads, which will actively rectify saltpeter production in the future. In addition, Manager Zeng has also proposed seven measures for reorganizing the Changlu salt affairs: 1. Management of salt fields: Fragmented and scattered salt fields should be consolidated, and ditches and roads should be dug and built around the outer perimeter of the salt fields to facilitate anti-smuggling. Field affairs offices and tax police stations should be established to manage the field property. 2. Management of abandoned salt fields: Roads should be built and police stations should be set up to prevent the concealment of bandits and maintain local security. 3. Management of local salt areas: As a short-term solution, widespread publicity should be conducted to discourage consumption and cooperate with local governments to strictly prohibit transportation and sale. Then, opportunities should be taken to destroy the pans and pools used to produce local salt. As a long-term solution, soil experts should be hired to test the technique of changing the properties of alkaline soil to benefit agriculture. 4. Management of Liaoning and Eastern smuggling: The customs should be requested to assist in investigating maritime smuggling, and police stations should be set up along the coast to serve as watchposts. 5. Reorganization of anti-smuggling efforts: The reorganization should be carried out by imitating the methods of the Lianghuai tax police. 6. Improvement of transportation merchants: The regulations for managing transportation merchants should be revised. The minimum quantity of salt to be transported per shipment should be set for each port, and transportation merchants should be held responsible for transporting the full amount. The selling price should be reviewed at any time, and the quality of salt should be inspected to reduce the burden on the people and benefit official sales. 7. Improving work efficiency: The management of salt mounds and salt fields should be the responsibility of the inspecting personnel from the auditing side and the field affairs personnel from the field offices, respectively. The Tanggu branch office should be abolished and a salt mound supervision office should be established to simplify the chain of command and facilitate command. All the above reorganization plans have been reviewed by the Salt Affairs Administration and the Chief Auditing Office and will be implemented in order. It can be predicted that official sales will be smooth and tax revenue will increase sharply in the future.

A Drug Manufacturing Organization Was Uncovered in Xuzhou; Seven People Jointly Manufactured Heroin; The Offender, Jiang ZhanKui, is Detained in the County Government 94

Xuzhou Correspondence: When Li Yannian was the garrison commander of Xuzhou some time ago, a large-scale drug manufacturing organization was uncovered. It was managed by well-known figures in Xuzhou. The manufacturing plant was located in the home of Zhang Weishun, a wealthy man in Yongcheng County. Li sent troops from the Ninth Division to arrest Zhang and also arrested Liu Bingchen, Ding Yinzhou, Cao Ziting, Jiang Zhankui, Wen Baoyu, etc. Liu and Ding fled quickly upon hearing the news. Cao, Jiang, and Wen were arrested successively. At that time, local people all advocated for strict punishment. However, Li was about to leave Xuzhou, so they were leniently sentenced to pay 100,000 yuan. Before the money could be paid, they were sent to the county prison. During the term of the previous County Magistrate Yu, the detainees requested bail to raise the money. They were released on bail one after another and paid a small amount of the gambling debt. Afterward, as time passed and circumstances changed, the fugitives secretly returned to Xuzhou. This case had been dormant for a long time. However, Jiang Zhankui, who was a leader of the mob, did not repent. After being released on bail, he colluded with many people to secretly set up a plant near Zifang Mountain in the Eastern Station area to manufacture heroin. It was stipulated that each person had one share, and each share was 500 yuan. There were as many as seven partners. There were two drug-making machines. The county government arrested two drug dealers, Dai Xiaochun and Chen Yuankui, and learned the inside story. County Magistrate Wang sent police officers to Jiang Zhankui's place, pretending to be Zhengzhou merchants who wanted to buy heroin for resale with 200 yuan in cash. Jiang thought they were in the same business and discussed the price back and forth. On the evening of the 12th, the money and goods were exchanged. Several other police officers lay in ambush outside the room. When the goods were delivered, they rushed in and arrested Jiang. He was taken to the county government for secret interrogation. Jiang confessed that he had set up a factory to make drugs. The shareholders were Zhao Shoushan of Sanduo Pharmacy, Mi Heng of Huabei Hotel, Cao Yunzhen, Wang Zhaoji of Jinpu Hotel, Liu Peiji of Jiangbei Restaurant, and Liu Xiwu, a resident of Zifang, totaling seven people. The two manufacturing machines were both located at Liu Xiwu's home, and Li Lantings was hired as a technician. The drug-making machines were purchased by Zhao and Cao in Shanghai. Using opium as raw material, they could produce fifty or sixty taels [unit of weight, approx. 1.3 oz] per day. They started manufacturing in October of last year, and the raw materials were purchased from the Tongguan area, etc. After hearing the confession, County Magistrate Wang immediately sent police officers with secret warrants to arrest each of the criminals in their homes and shops. However, all the criminals had fled upon hearing the news. Only drugs and sundries were found in Liu Xiwu's home, and the drug-making machines had also been dismantled and hidden. Jiang is currently detained in the county government, and the remaining criminals are still being hunted. Local people attach great importance to this case and advocate strict legal action. (16th)

Songjiang: Continued Report on the Lantern Parade Incident Causing Trouble 95

Villagers near Tinglin, because of the dragon lantern parade, disobeyed the prohibition of the Public Security Bureau branch, which led to the destruction of the Public Security Bureau branch in the town. It is now learned that since the district office and the public security organs convened a meeting with the heads of various towns and villages, the villagers Gu A'gen, Gu A'wu, Jiang Kunquan, and others were arrested, identified as the main culprits, and sent to the county bureau for legal action. As a result, the farmers near the town have all fled, which will hinder spring plowing. According to villagers from the area who came to Songjiang to report the situation, the three men were beaten by the police after being detained by the sub-bureau. However, it is still doubtful whether the three men are indeed the perpetrators of the lantern parade incident. Therefore, Mei Shuibu, the head of the district, has submitted a request to the county government, asking that innocent people not be implicated to avoid hindering spring farming.

Suzhou: Detailed Account of Qiu Chunwu's Suicide 96

Qiu Chunwu, a Suzhou native who is currently working as a clerk at the Shanghai Gold Exchange, suddenly committed suicide by hitting himself on the railway tracks near the Zhenru station a few days ago. His brains splattered, and his death was very tragic. His coffin was transported to Suzhou on the 16th. The details of the case are recorded below. Qiu, whose courtesy name is Wu Hong and who is also known as Shu Bin, is 22 years old. He has four brothers, and he and his second brother are currently working at the Gold Exchange, enjoying a comfortable life. His home is located at No. 115 Xiangfu Temple Lane in Suzhou. His father's name is Rong Sheng, and his family has a small amount of land. Qiu and his brothers were born to his father's concubine, Madam Wang. He liked Peking Opera and often went to the Shanghai Datong Peking Opera Club in his spare time. About three weeks ago, Qiu and several friends went to visit the Wusong Fort. At that time, a hurricane suddenly arose, blowing Qiu's mud hat into the Pudong beach. Qiu was about to bend down to pick it up when another gust of wind came, causing Qiu to lose his footing and fall into the river. Fortunately, he was familiar with the water and did not drown. He then returned to Suzhou to rest. On the eighth of this month, he went to Shanghai to work. On the twelfth, his second brother returned to Suzhou for business. Later, he suddenly went missing. The staff in his office sent a letter to Suzhou to inquire whether Qiu had returned home. Qiu's family was extremely panicked (because according to the rules of the office, the two brothers could not ask for leave at the same time unless there was a special accident). They replied to the office and asked them to investigate on their behalf. However, on the afternoon of the next day (the 13th), Qiu's family suddenly received a telegram from the Nanxiang District Office, stating that a young man was found near Jilu Lane, Cheng Ba Tu, Shenghua Township, near the Beijing-Shanghai Railway near Zhenru, wearing a camel hair robe, covered with a blue cloth shirt, twill pants, and yellow-striped leather shoes, died there, hoping to come and identify him quickly. His brother received the telegram and went to check with his uncle Xifan on the same day. They saw that it was indeed Qiu's body and found a suicide note addressed to his parents next to him. It briefly stated that he had no choice but to take this path, but it was not for economic reasons, not for love, and not related to friends. He expressed his gratitude for their upbringing and said that he would repay them in the next life. He asked them to take care of themselves and not to be sad about his death, etc. He then asked the local county government for permission to waive an autopsy and transported the coffin back to Suzhou. The reason for his suicide is still unknown.

Wuxi: Active Factory Inspections Are Underway 97

In order to improve factory management and increase factory production, the Ministry of Industry has decided to implement factory inspections in stages, with a five-year deadline. Wuxi, as the county with the most factories in the interior of Jiangsu Province, is particularly difficult to promote. Therefore, the Ministry of Industry has specially dispatched Han Xicheng, Secretary of the Central Factory Inspection Office, and Cheng Qijun, Factory Inspection Commissioner of the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department, to come to Wuxi to discuss with County Magistrate Yan and Bureau Chief Zhang of the Construction Bureau. It has been decided to start with the cotton spinning and flour industries. The Chamber of Commerce has been invited to send letters to various factories in the two industries, asking them to send responsible representatives to a meeting at the County Chamber of Commerce on the afternoon of the 17th to discuss the implementation procedures. Yesterday afternoon, Bureau Chief Zhang of the Construction Bureau accompanied the two commissioners from the Ministry and the Province to attend the meeting. The textile industry was represented by seven factories, including Shenxin, Qingfeng, Guangqin, Zhenxin, Yukang, Lixin, and Yeqin. The flour industry was represented by four factories, including Maoxin No. 1 and No. 2, Jiufeng, and Tailong. First, Mr. Han explained the factory inspection system. The first to pilot the system was the United Kingdom, which has a history of more than 100 years. Subsequently, countries around the world have followed suit and achieved good results. The Chinese government, in order to improve its international standing and develop its industrial plans, has formulated the Factory Inspection Law in order to implement it step by step. At present, governments in various provinces and cities are actively carrying it out. The Shanghai Chinese Concession factories have been inspected by Tian Heqing and others sent by the municipal government. Zhejiang, Shandong, Henan, Yunnan, Qingdao, Tianjin, Hankou, Weihaiwei, and other places are also making efforts by the respective provincial and municipal governments, and the results are good. Wuxi is a factory area, which is related to the expectations of China and foreign countries. This work really cannot be delayed any longer. The current needs of the environment should be carefully reviewed, and the implementation procedures for factory inspection should be formulated. The order of priority should be determined according to the urgency, difficulty, and ease of implementation, so that it is easier to promote and achieve practical results. Finally, the method of starting inspections of various factories was discussed, and the meeting adjourned.

Changshu: A Major Fire at Canghai Temple on Yushan Mountain 98

On the 16th of this month (the 3rd day of the 3rd month of the lunar calendar), according to local customs, there has been a custom of pilgrimage on this day since the Ming Dynasty. The incense societies from various villages all take the Xuan Di Ancestral Temple in Canghai Temple on the top of Yushan Mountain outside the west gate as their destination. On this day, the pilgrimage is no less crowded than the Tianzhu Temple in Hangzhou. However, this year it is even more prosperous than in the past. Pilgrims and spectators, from the west gate to Ancestor Mountain, a distance of about five miles by land and water, are all walking one after another. And the monks in the entire temple on the mountain rely on the income of this one day for their food and clothing for the year. However, on the night of this day, the pilgrims scattered. The monks in the temple were cleaning up and tidying up, and they did not go to sleep until 3 a.m. on the 17th. After a while, they were suddenly awakened by the sound of wood exploding. They quickly put on their clothes and got up to look. They suddenly saw that the Great Compassion Hall in the back was on fire, and the fire was very fierce. However, there were no neighbors in the mountains, and they could not call for help. Moreover, there was a lack of firefighting equipment on the mountain, and there was no way to draw water. Therefore, they could only sit and watch. It was not until dawn that hundreds of villagers from the foot of the mountain climbed up to extinguish the fire. The burned buildings include the Great Compassion Hall, Amitabha Pavilion, Wenchang Pavilion, East and West guest rooms, and the main kitchen. Except for the main hall and the Hall of Three Lives Buddhas, the remaining dozens of temple buildings were all reduced to ashes. However, the amount of loss this time is particularly shocking. Just the income on that day was about 3,000 taels of silver. In addition, there were various utensils and miscellaneous items donated by various incense societies, as well as hundreds of paintings and calligraphy by famous figures from ancient and modern times in the temple. The total is estimated to be around 30,000 taels of silver. It is also known that during the fire, two temple keepers, because they had not slept for many days and were extremely tired, did not wake up in time to escape and were buried in the fire. One was 55 years old, and the other was 15 years old. The situation was extremely tragic. Now, the abbot of the temple, Monk Zhiguang, is extremely anxious.

Changzhou: Re-registration for Adding Rickshaws 99

The Wu County Government previously planned to add 300 rickshaws, including 100 in the city area and 200 on various roads, inviting merchants to register and claim them. Each rickshaw was required to pay a car price of 60 yuan and a public welfare donation of 120 yuan. Later, because no one took it up, it was submitted to the province for approval. It was ordered to cancel the distinction between urban and rural areas and re-register within a limited time. County Magistrate Cai specifically raised the matter for general discussion at the administrative meeting on the 16th. The resolution is excerpted below: 1. The Provincial Department ordered the registration of 300 vehicles. According to the needs of local transactions, half of them will be released first. For example, if 10 licenses are received, 5 will be released first, and so on. 2. Each vehicle will pay a public welfare donation of 120 yuan, and the price of each vehicle is 80 yuan, which will be deposited in the bank for verification. 3. The vehicles will be changed to chartered cars, and the style will be specified by the third section of the county government and manufactured accordingly. 4. When existing vehicles are inspected, if they are found to be old and unsuitable for riding, they should be ordered to be renovated according to the new style within a limited time. Otherwise, the license will be revoked and compensated by vehicles that have received new licenses but have not yet taken to the streets. 5. If the registration exceeds the quota, it will be determined by drawing lots. 6. The registration date is from April 21st to April 23rd.

Guo Chengjiu, the former director of the Two Lakes Special Tax Bureau, raped a young girl, Zhou Zhuoying. Guo himself died of illness at the time of the incident. Subsequently, the prosecutor refused to accept the acquittal and appealed to the Supreme Court, which sent the case back for retrial. Japanese Envoy Arichi Visited Huang Fu Yesterday, Conversed For Quite Some Time; Suzuki Also Went To Visit 115

Friends and relatives in Shanghai went to visit him one after another. He plans to stay in Shanghai for a short time and then return to his hometown to sweep the tombs before going to Mogan Mountain for a temporary stay. Mr. Huang's activities yesterday were as follows:

Guests Visiting 118

Mayor Wu and Wang Jingqi, the former envoy to Belgium, also visited one after another yesterday morning. As Mr. Huang was conferring with the Japanese envoy, they hastily declined and left without meeting him. At 3:00 p.m. yesterday, Mr. Huang received the Belgian envoy Ji Youmu at his residence, which was a normal visit and did not have any special mission.

Arichi’s Comments 119

According to the Japanese newspaper "Shanghai Daily Evening Edition" published yesterday, Envoy Arichi, accompanied by interpreter Ono, went to Huang's residence on Qiqi Road at 9:05 a.m. today (the 17th) for a conference of approximately one and a half hours. Lieutenant General Suzuki also went to Huang's residence at 10:15 a.m. and did not leave until 12:30 p.m. According to Envoy Arichi, after meeting with Mr. Huang, he made the following statement to the Japanese press corps: "Today's visit included listening to explanations on the situation of the Nanchang Conference and the overall situation of Chinese politics. Mr. Huang fully understands the Sino-Japanese relationship and strives to adjust the Chinese side's implementation and resolution of issues such as the opening of traffic and mail. This requires full consideration. However, this issue is not originally a local issue, but a fundamental understanding of the Sino-Japanese relationship. This matter has gradually become more favorable than last year, so promoting it will be even more beneficial. In the near future, new problems will arise between China and Japan." It is heard that Envoy Arichi plans to return to his country on the Ryuta Maru on the 21st or the Shanghai Maru on the 25th.

Newspaper Reports 120

Yesterday, the Japanese newspaper "Mainichi Shimbun" reported that the head of the Beiping Political Affairs Committee, Huang Fu, according to a telegram from the Chinese side, had adopted a negative attitude. In reality, Huang did not show any pessimism due to the positive outcome of the Nanchang Conference. After meeting with Chinese news reporters, stock market prices surged. In response to questions from the press corps, he stated, "My mission is small, but its impact on China is significant. It aims to save the two nations of East Asia. During the Nanchang Conference, I reported on the past six months' developments and current situation in North China." Regarding the issues of through traffic and postal services, he said, "Both Japan and China attach great importance to this. From my perspective, there are no practical inconveniences." However, Huang avoided specific details. Regarding the establishment of customs, he criticized the Chinese media for insufficient understanding. As for the issue of resignation, he said, "Considering the overall situation, I fear that my resignation would further destabilize North China."

Shanghai's Foreign Trade in the First Quarter Shows a Deficit of Over 100 Million Yuan 121

According to Shenshi News Agency, the Jianghai Customs announced yesterday that the import value for March was 65,636,050 yuan, and the export value was 19,035,915 yuan, resulting in a deficit of 46,600,135 yuan. This is a decrease of 8,965,601 yuan compared to the deficit of 55,565,736 yuan in the same period last year, but a sharp increase of 18,610,567 yuan compared to the previous month. The total import and export value for March was 84,671,965 yuan, an increase of 19,345,378 yuan compared to the previous month, and a decrease of 20,067,174 yuan compared to the same period last year.

Spring Deficit Exceeds 100 Million Yuan 122

According to statistics released on the foreign trade situation in Shanghai for the first quarter of this year (January to March), imports totaled 177,491,343 yuan, a decrease of 32,628,883 yuan compared to the same period last year. Exports totaled 61,900,375 yuan, a decrease of 22,398,748 yuan compared to the same period last year. The total deficit for the first quarter was 115,550,968 yuan, a decrease of 10,230,134 yuan compared to the same period last year. The total import and export trade value was 239,431,718 yuan, a decrease of 55,027,631 yuan compared to 294,459,349 yuan in the same period last year.

Imports and Exports in the First Quarter 123

The main items in Shanghai's foreign trade for the first quarter of this year were: In terms of imports, raw cotton, metals and minerals, machinery, and metal products all increased compared to last year; woolen products, silk fabrics, aquatic and marine products, wheat, rice, sugar, petroleum, and coal all decreased. In terms of exports, animals and animal products, ramie, and miscellaneous goods saw slight increases; leather, oils, tea, silk fabrics, and minerals all saw significant decreases.

New Clues Found in China Aviation Company Plane Crash Yesterday: Fishermen Recovered Lost Mailbags in the Waters Off Huangmang Mountain, Zhenhai County; Reports of Finding the Plane Are Misleading 124

According to Shenshi News Agency, the China Aviation Company's No. 17 Sikorsky aircraft has been missing for a week. Yesterday morning, two mailbags scattered from the crashed plane were discovered in the waters off Zhenhai. The mailbags were recovered by a fisherman surnamed Zhang in the waters off Huangmang Mountain near Zhenhai. After receiving this information, the company sent Alison and two others by plane to search the area yesterday. They returned to Shanghai at around 3:00 PM, but no new discoveries were made. It is generally speculated that the plane has undoubtedly sunk and been destroyed at sea. The company will hire boats starting today to conduct a detailed search in the waters near Zhenhai. The reports yesterday from Hangzhou stating that the missing plane had been found were misleading. Details are as follows:

Discovery of Scattered Mail from Missing Plane 125

At 9:00 AM yesterday, the China Aviation Company received two bags of mail scattered from the No. 16 missing plane, brought in by the Xinjiang Tianlun steamer. The items were recovered on the morning of the day after the plane went missing (i.e., the 11th) by fisherman Zhang Huixi while fishing near Huangmang Mountain, five miles from Zhenhai. After realizing that they were from the China Aviation Company's missing plane, they were handed over to Lin Jiexian, who was left in Zhenhai with the damaged No. 19 plane. Lin then entrusted the Xinjiang Tianlun steamer to bring them to Shanghai with a letter. This is the process of the discovery. The items included a yellow canvas official mailbag from the China Aviation Company with the word "Swatow" written on it in English, containing a book of China Aviation Company passenger tickets, two daily postal transport report forms, one daily passenger ticket report form, and an English pilot report form. All of the above items were intended for use by the company's Fuzhou station. In addition, there was a small white postal bag from the Postal Administration with the words "Shanghai No. 45-394" written on it, containing a small box of rubber nipples for baby milk bottles, sent by the Ke Fa Pharmacy in Shanghai to the Fuzhou station. All of the above items had water stains and yellow mud marks due to being washed by seawater.

Another Plane Dispatched Yesterday to Search and Track 126

After learning of this clue, the China Aviation Company consulted and decided to send pilot Alison in a Lockheed aircraft at 11:00 AM yesterday, along with Gleeson and Chinese mechanic Mr. Gao, to search the waters near Huangmang Mountain and the surrounding islands, hoping for further new discoveries. They then flew to Zhenhai and landed. Gleeson and Mr. Gao stayed in Zhenhai and hired a boat with Mr. Lin this morning, along with the fisherman who found the mail, to search the waters near Zhenhai and the surrounding islands, hoping to find other clues. Alison flew back to Shanghai by plane at 3:30 PM in the afternoon.

General Speculation: People and Plane All Sank 127

Based on the lost items found yesterday, it is speculated that the missing plane and its passengers have all perished without a doubt. Moreover, the fuselage must have shattered upon entering the water; otherwise, the mail would have been difficult to discover. However, according to Manager Dai of the China Aviation Company, speaking to a reporter from Shenshi News Agency, they still have one last hope: that the passengers may have been rescued by fishermen on nearby islands, but due to injuries and language barriers, they were unable to immediately send news. However, this is just a hope against all odds. The company will make further efforts to search in the coming days, regardless of life or death, in order to bring the matter to a conclusion.

Board Meeting to Improve Flight Routes 128

After the plane crash, the company has decided to hold a full board meeting at 5:00 PM this Friday to discuss all follow-up issues. At the same time, how to ensure the safety and improvement of China Aviation's existing routes will also be discussed separately. According to a company announcement yesterday, the Shanghai-Guangdong route will be actively resumed, and new aircraft will be purchased from the United States in the coming days. Whether to continue using Sikorsky aircraft or purchase other types will be decided after the board meeting.

Reports of Finding the Aviation School Plane Are Misleading 129

According to the Shanghai Aviation News Agency, the reports yesterday from Hangzhou stating that the missing plane had been found by the aviation school are completely false. The plane found in the waters near the Weiyuan Fort in Zhenhai was actually the No. 40 plane, which was forced to land and damaged while searching for the missing plane. Furthermore, the reports that passenger numbers on the company's Shanghai-Hankou and Shanghai-Beiping routes have decreased due to the Shanghai-Guangdong plane crash are not entirely accurate. Even before the plane crash, there were often periods of low passenger numbers on these two routes. Moreover, the Shanghai-Hankou route flies along the river, allowing for safe landings at any time, and the stations are close together, making it convenient to report weather conditions and inspect aircraft. The Shanghai-Beiping route has never experienced any unfortunate incidents, and the company plans to purchase new aircraft to operate on this route in order to reduce flight time.

Central Aviation School Clarification 130

A telegram from Hangzhou states: All newspapers have reported that the school's aircraft found the missing Sikorsky aircraft belonging to the China Aviation Company, which is not true. Although the school dispatched aircraft for reconnaissance, no findings were made. This is hereby clarified. Central Aviation School Seal.

Ministry of Communications Newly Revised Regulations for Joint Postal and Telegraph Offices; Strict Orders Issued to All Locations for Strict Compliance 132

According to New Sound News Agency, in order to facilitate the development of postal services for the people, the Ministry of Communications has specially formulated regulations for the joint establishment of postal and telegraph offices and has issued strict orders to the Directorate General of Posts and the relevant telegraph bureaus to comply with the contents of the regulations. The original texts of the Ministry's orders to Shanghai and other postal and telegraph offices yesterday are recorded separately below.

Joint Establishment Plan: The most important aspects of the joint establishment regulations are the following two: (1) Telegraph bureaus of the third class or below in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hebei provinces shall all be jointly established with local post offices. (2) Telegraph receiving offices shall be set up in all postal branches in major commercial ports throughout the country, and postal branches shall be set up in all telegraph bureau receiving and dispatching offices (note: the major commercial ports referred to have been designated by the Ministry of Communications as Shanghai, Nanjing, Beiping, Tianjin, Hankou, Qingdao, Chongqing, Xiamen, Changsha, Shantou, Zhangjiakou, Yichang, Fuzhou, Xi'an, Ningbo, Yantai, Guiyang, Jinan, Wanxian, Wuhu, Zhengzhou, Lanzhou, Shashi, Guangzhou, Nanchang, Chengdu, Suiyuan, Hangzhou, Taiyuan, Xuzhou, Anqing, Wenzhou, Jiujiang, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, Quanzhou, Bengbu, Wuzhou, Nanning, Wuchang, Changde, Baoding, Kunming, Qinhuangdao, Kaifeng, and Shijiazhuang, a total of 47 locations). Currently, all locations have begun to implement the first regulation separately. Regarding the second regulation, all locations have made excuses such as small houses and unsuitable locations to delay and postpone implementation. The establishment of telegraph receiving offices in post offices has not been widespread, and the establishment of postal branches in telegraph bureau receiving and dispatching offices is even rarer.

Newly Revised Regulations: In order to promote new policies and benefit the people, the Ministry of Communications yesterday (the 17th) specially stipulated three regulations and ordered all postal and telegraph bureaus to comply: (1) Postal bureaus and their branches in Shanghai and other places must universally establish telegraph receiving and dispatching offices, regardless of grade, without exception. If the postal branch houses are too small to accommodate them, they should be relocated to suitable houses in order to be jointly established with the nearest telegraph bureau or receiving and dispatching office. The receiving and dispatching office may also be equipped with a telegraph machine. (2) Telegraph bureaus in Shanghai and other places must universally establish postal branches. If the houses are too small, they should be relocated to suitable houses in order to be jointly established with the nearest post office or postal branch. (3) The original receiving and dispatching offices of telegraph bureaus in Shanghai and other places should be abolished. Those that are allowed to be retained due to special circumstances, such as important locations and special business connections, must still have postal branches set up by the post office, without exception. The Ministry of Communications has strictly ordered all relevant bureaus to strictly comply with the above three regulations. Those who make excuses to delay will be dealt with for dereliction of duty.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company New "Four Seas" Ships Officially Named: Hai Yuan, Hai Heng, Hai Li, Hai Zhen; Design Logos Also Drawn Up; To Be Sent to England Immediately for Manufacturing According to the Style 133

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company used Sino-British Boxer Indemnity funds to order four "Four Seas" ships from England to expand the South China shipping routes. Wu Damming and Shi Gan were specially sent to London to supervise the construction, which has already begun. The first batch of two ships is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at the end of September, and the second batch of two ships is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at the end of December. The ship names and application designs for the new ships were finalized by the company yesterday and sent to the Jianghai Customs for inquiries. There were no duplicates. The ship names, etc., will be sent to England immediately for manufacturing according to the style. The situation is described as follows:

New Ship Names Finalized: The names of the four new ships ordered by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company in London were initially drafted by the company's secretariat and shipping department with the characters "Guo" (National), "Hua" (China), and "Hai" (Sea) and submitted to the board of directors for selection. After discussion by the board of directors, it was decided that since the two recently purchased Norwegian ships used the names "Hai Rui" and "Hai Xiang," the four new "Four Seas" ships should also be named with the character "Hai." They were changed to "Hai Yuan," "Hai Heng," "Hai Li," and "Hai Zhen" as the names of the four new ships. After formal approval by the board of directors, they were sent to the shipping department and forwarded to Wu and Shi in London.

Customs Reply: Names Can Be Used 134

The shipping department, noting that many Chinese merchant ships in recent years have used names with the character "Hai," had to inquire in advance to determine whether the four new ship names were the same as those of other ships. They sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs, which replied yesterday that after a thorough search of incoming and outgoing ships, there were no names identical to these four new ship names, and they could be used.

Design of the Character "挻" (Shun) 135

The ship names, due to the large size of the ships, must be six feet square. Qian Jinding of the shipping department wrote out the eight characters "Hai Yuan," "Hai Heng," "Hai Li," and "Hai Zhen" yesterday in preparation for sending them to Wu to have them placed on the outer hull of the ships in the same style. The design logos for all items used on the new ships were also drafted by the company and consist of a round shape resembling a lifebuoy with the national flag and the company flag crossed in the middle, the five characters "Guo Ying Zhao Shang Ju" (National China Merchants Steam Navigation Company) horizontally above, and a shape resembling a sailor's belt drawn below. However, there are no English characters in the design. It was drawn up yesterday and will be sent to London along with the ship names for manufacturing.

Crew and Technicians to Go to England in Batches 136

The "Hai Yuan" and "Hai Heng" are the first two new ships to be built. The company-assigned crew and technicians who need to go to England to practice on the new ship machinery have already provided their resumes and submitted them to the Ministry of Communications. As soon as the approval order arrives in Shanghai, technician and director of the Inland China Merchants Factory Huang Zonglun, chief engineer of the Jiahe ship Li Guoquan, two third engineers, and two marine engineering students selected from the Wusong Merchant Marine School will be sent to the British shipyard for practice first. It is planned that these six people will go abroad by early May at the latest. Captains Ma Jiajun and Teng Shibiao, who will go to pick up the ships, will be sent to England from Shanghai in July.

Minqiang Ship Sinks After Hitting Reef; Entire Ship Submerged in River; Cargo Also Lost with Ship 137

Recently, the water level of the Sichuan River has risen sharply, making navigation even more difficult for ships on the upper Yangtze River. With even slight carelessness, ships may hit reefs. A foreign merchant ship company in Shanghai received a telegram from Yichang yesterday stating that the Minsheng Company's Minqiang ship suddenly hit a reef above Yichang. The ship's hull was damaged, and it sank completely before rescue could be carried out. This matter is of great importance. The situation is as follows:

Difficult Navigation Due to Rising Water in Sichuan River 138

The Sichuan River waterway in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, from Yichang to Chongqing, is the most difficult to navigate. There are numerous dangerous shoals in the river, making navigation very dangerous. During the low water period, it is easier to see the shoals. From the first of this month, the river water has been rising daily, and the submerged reefs and beaches are covered by the river water. If the river pilot is even slightly careless, the ship's hull may hit a submerged reef. Therefore, upper Yangtze River ships regard this "insufficiently risen water" period as the most difficult period for Sichuan River ship navigation.

The Minqiang Ship Hits a Reef 139

Currently, the Minsheng Company has the most ships navigating the Sichuan River. Their routes are divided into the Shanghai-Chongqing and Yichang-Chongqing routes. The Minqiang ship, with a deadweight of 200 tons, is used for Shanghai-Chongqing navigation during the low water period and operates on the Chongqing-Yichang route during the high water period. This time, it was loaded with cargo and passengers from Chongqing. On the 15th of this month, the ship was passing through the Shiguan Shoal. After passing the shoal, it sailed to the Xintan River surface, where there are many submerged reefs (above Miaohua, opposite Yaowan). It was also during the rising water period, and there was fog. The pilot's careless navigation caused the ship's hull to hit a submerged reef on the Xintan River. The water rushed in quickly, and the ship's hull immediately broke.

Entire Ship Submerged in the River 140

After the Minqiang ship broke, river water rushed into the cabin madly. Because the cargo was loaded in each cabin, the ship sank immediately due to the heavy load and the reef. Yesterday afternoon, Shanghai received a telegram from Yichang stating that after the Minqiang ship hit a reef in Xintan, the bottom of the cabin was severely damaged, and it could not be rescued. The ship's hull was completely submerged in the river.

Number of Losses Unknown 141

The cargo loaded in the ship also sank into the river with the ship. All crew members, sailors, and passengers on board fled for their lives in sampans and other small boats. Some were rescued by passing civilian boats, sailboats, and merchant ships. The Chongqing Minsheng Company headquarters has also dispatched ships to the site of the accident for rescue. As for cargo losses and crew and passenger injuries, it is currently unknown. Detailed reports are expected in the next day or two.

Social Bureau and Others Convened Silk Factory Businessmen Yesterday to Discuss Relief Measures; Instructed Both Sides to Report the Details of the Decline 144

China's silk industry has been affected by the dumping of Japanese silk in the European and American markets. The market price of Chinese silk has been falling sharply, resulting in huge losses for silk factories and workers. Silk factory owners and workers have requested relief from the Ministry of Industry and other departments. Duck Industry Experiences Market Suspension Crisis; Chicken and Duck Dealers Arbitrarily Changed the Three-Seven Foreign Exchange Rate; Telegrams Sent to Various Ports to Stop Loading Ducks to Shanghai 145

The Shanghai chicken and duck industry and the duck slaughtering industry have experienced a market suspension dispute due to the issue of three-seven foreign exchange rate payment. The details are as follows:

Cause of the Dispute: Duck slaughterers purchase ducks from chicken and duck dealers and pay for them with 30 yuan of corner silver for every 100 yuan (10 corners equal one yuan), which is the so-called three-seven foreign exchange rate. This has been used for more than 30 years. In 1930, there was a dispute, which was later resolved by the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau convening representatives from the two industry associations to sign a commercial dispute settlement record. The record was divided into two articles: (1) Except for the Nandefeng and Xinchangshun chicken and duck dealers, which all use silver dollars, the other dealers will still use the three-seven foreign exchange rate calculation, because the Nandefeng and Xinchangshun dealers have open spaces in their stores where they can store ducks, allowing vendors to buy and slaughter them at any time, which is more convenient than other dealers who need to feed the ducks. (2) After the settlement case is signed, if any members of the industry do not comply, the two industry associations may jointly decide on measures to ban them in a joint meeting and submit them to the Social Bureau for record and implementation. After the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the chicken and duck dealers changed to collecting money in silver dollars. At that time, the duck slaughterers sent representatives to negotiate with the association, but it was ineffective. They submitted a request to the Municipal Social Bureau for mediation, but there was no result. Therefore, they convened a members' meeting on April 8 to discuss solutions.

Triggering the Crisis: The meeting concluded by requesting the Chicken and Duck Association to show mutual aid and love and continue to sell at the three-seven foreign exchange rate. However, the Chicken and Duck Association replied that the customer did not agree and could not comply. Moreover, those chicken and duck dealers who were willing to sell at the three-seven foreign exchange rate were stopped by Zhao Songge, chairman of the Chicken and Duck Association, and telegrams were sent to various ports north of the Yangtze River to stop loading ducks to Shanghai. Those that had already been loaded and shipped to Shanghai were also ordered to be loaded back onto the original ships. As a result, duck slaughterers were forced to suspend business, and the crisis expanded.

The result was deemed satisfactory, and they left. Unexpectedly, a notice was sent today stating that our factory should pay a total of 70 yuan in inspection fees and other expenses annually, which is very surprising. It is found that the issue of factory inspection rights in the Shanghai Concession has not yet been resolved, and the French Concession authorities are using their power and influence to oppress factories and demand payment of inspection fees. If they refuse to pay, they are weak and powerless. If they reluctantly pay, it concerns the entire national sovereignty. The factory is in a畸形 state, and it is difficult to advance or retreat. Although the association is a legal industrial and commercial group, it is our duty to protect the factories of our members, but we still need to rely on the Yuan to hold a strong position and urge the municipal government to file a protest as soon as possible so that the strength is sufficient to withdraw the factory inspection fee and avoid losing sovereignty. The situation of last year's protest by the association against the Public Concession authorities ordering factories to improve and relocate is detailed in the book 'Industrial Safety and Management,' which is sent separately. Please review. Shanghai Machine-Made Domestic Goods Factory United Association bows."

French Far East Naval Commander, Vice-Admiral Tai Gude, Dies on Ship 148

Havas News Agency, Shanghai, 17th: The newly appointed French Far East Naval Commander, Vice-Admiral Tai Gude, was traveling north from Vietnam aboard the cruiser "Primauguet". He was originally scheduled to arrive this afternoon, but Mr. Tai developed pneumonia. At 5:50 this morning, he passed away despite medical treatment. It is reported that Mr. Tai was born on May 2, 1879. At the age of eighteen, he entered the Naval Academy. In 1900 (the year of Gengzi), he was dispatched to China. Subsequently, he came to China twice between 1910 and 1913. During the European War, he commanded torpedo boats in the Aegean Sea and fought in several battles. After the armistice, he served as a commander in the Atlantic and Mediterranean fleets and held important positions in the Naval General Staff. In 1927, he was appointed Director of General Affairs of the Ministry of the Navy. In 1928, he was promoted to Vice-Admiral and subsequently served as Chief of Staff of the Fortress Command. On October 17th of last year, he was appointed Commander of the Far East Fleet.

Zhejiang Tea Enters the Market and is Shipped to Shanghai 149

New tea produced in the mountains of Zhejiang's Hangzhou and surrounding areas has now entered the market. It is packaged into basket tea or wrapped tea and transported to Shanghai via the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway by various transport companies. This has always been a large volume. These box teas are expected to arrive in Shanghai around mid-May. Dongjiadu Ferry Operators Self-Managing Ferry Services: A Summary from the Pudong Fellow Villagers Association, Why Must the Xingye Trust Company Compete? 151

The Pudong Fellow Villagers Association submitted a summary to the Shanghai Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government regarding the Dongjiadu ferry operators raising funds to self-manage ferry services. The document reads: "Respectfully summarizing, this association previously received a letter from the Dongjiadu ferry industry requesting that the Municipal Government be asked to allow the original ferry operators to raise funds to self-manage the improvement of ferry services. This was submitted by this association, but was not approved. The ferry operators, fearing that they would be unemployed and lose their livelihoods, submitted another request. I, Yong, with respect for my hometown, which has always been valued, must speak on behalf of my fellow villagers to our Party Department and Mayor. In my humble opinion, it is more appropriate and proper for Dongjiadu to be managed by the original ferry operators raising funds. Let me explain the reasons: The purpose of improving ferry services is to facilitate the public. If this purpose can be achieved, it is acceptable for the city to manage it, and even more acceptable for the people to manage it. If the Dongjiadu ferry must be managed by the Xingye Trust Company, disregarding the original ferry operators, it would appear to be using political power to compete with the people for profit. This is the first reason. Under party rule, the government aims to implement the Three Principles of the People, and the Principle of People's Livelihood is one of the Three Principles. Administrators should always consider this. If the Dongjiadu ferry must be managed by the Xingye Trust Company, hundreds of families who directly or indirectly depend on the original ferry operators for their livelihoods will become unemployed, which is contrary to the Principle of People's Livelihood. This is the second reason. According to the regulations on supervising privately-operated public utilities promulgated by the National Government, and the ferry regulations promulgated by the Municipal Government, privately-operated ferries are not absolutely prohibited. This applies even to newly established businesses. The Dongjiadu ferry industry, which has a history of hundreds of years, should be allowed to convert to ferry services. From a legal perspective, there is no conflict. This is the third reason. When the Municipal Government manages municipal affairs, using its own power results in small achievements, while using the power of the people results in great achievements. Since the original ferry operators are willing to raise funds to self-manage the Dongjiadu ferry, granting them permission would be a good use of the people's power, making it easier for municipal public utilities to develop. This is the fourth reason. The government should focus on major and long-term issues. The navigation rights of our country are mostly controlled by foreigners, and recovering them for self-management is a major and long-term issue. The Dongjiadu ferry is a minor and short-term issue. If the people have the ability to self-manage it, then let them do so, and the Xingye Trust Company should focus on major and long-term issues that the people cannot handle. This is the fifth reason. The government is the government of the people, and the Party Department announces to the citizens that all citizens should hear it together. The government is the government of the people. Any measure that benefits the people should be implemented even if it has not been formally approved. Conversely, any measure that is detrimental to the people should be revised even if it has been formally approved. If the Dongjiadu ferry is transferred to the Xingye Trust Company, hundreds of families who directly or indirectly depend on it for their livelihoods will become unemployed, which is greatly detrimental to the people. Although the Municipal Government has approved the company's proposal, the ferry operators' petition has been pending for a long time. The documents are available for review. Moreover, the people's ferry is to facilitate the people's travel, and the ferry for the people's travel should be allowed to be self-managed by the people. The Trust Company should have many other businesses to manage, so why must it compete for this? Changing course for profit is a common practice for politicians. This is the sixth reason. The Dongjiadu ferry industry dates back to the eighth year of the Shunzhi reign of the former Qing Dynasty, lasting hundreds of years. Hundreds of families, and thousands of men, women, and children, directly or indirectly depend on it for their livelihoods. It has a long history and a broad impact. In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, Huang Zihe, who had no historical connection with Dongjiadu, petitioned to take over the management and was approved. Now, the original ferry operators, who have a history of hundreds of years with Dongjiadu, are requesting to self-manage it, but are being denied permission. In terms of reason and sentiment, how can this be considered fair? This is the seventh reason. The Municipal Government approved the association's submission, stating that after the Xingye Trust Company manages the Dongjiadu ferry, it will still allow the ferry industry to operate in consideration of the ferry industry. From the surface, it seems to be taking everything into consideration, but in reality, it will result in mutual damage. The lesson of Qingning Temple is still fresh. If the operation is still allowed, why not just improve it? The Trust Company can also avoid some losses. Some may say that the weak ferry operators, with their old-fashioned ferries, cannot compete with the powerful Xingye Trust Company and its modern ferries. This kind of approach is nominally considerate, but actually ridiculous. It is not a groundless worry. The government should set an example for the people and should not do this. This is the eighth reason. Some may say that after the Xingye Trust Company manages the ferry, the original Dongjiadu ferry workers can still be employed. However, this approach can only save a portion of the ferry workers and cannot save most of the ferry operators. Even for the small number of rescued ferry workers, the power of hiring and firing is in the hands of others, and the foundation is not secure, causing great concern. This is the ninth reason. The Xingye Trust Company was established using a portion of the Reconstruction Public Bonds. Its mission should be to rebuild Zhabei, which was destroyed by the violent Japanese, in order to fulfill the purpose of establishing the company. Now, without hearing any plans for the reconstruction of Zhabei, it is first plotting to seize the livelihood of the Dongjiadu ferry industry, so that those who want to revitalize the people's business are instead destroying the people's business. Isn't this contrary to the true purpose of establishing the company? This is the tenth reason. In summary of the above reasons, I sincerely request the Party Department and the Mayor to accept the opinions of the ferry operators of the original ferry, allow them to raise funds to self-manage, emphasize the people's livelihood, and conform to party rule. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Party Department, Mayor Wu, Du Yong, Chairman of the Pudong Fellow Villagers Association, April 13, Year 23."

Fire in Menghua Lou Street Burns Girl to Death: The Whole Family Jumped Out of the Window, Girl Meidi Could Not be Carried Out 152

Yesterday at 9:15 AM, a fire broke out in the home of Gu Liansheng, a native of Zhoushan, who lived in the front building at No. 2 Yifeng Lane, Lane 123, Menghua Lou Street, Nanshi.
