During a Sleepless Night, a Man was Severed at the Head with a Kitchen Knife: Chen Youxing Cut Wu Dongsheng, Lu Quansheng was Implicated but Denies it 154

Wu Dongsheng, a native of Ningbo, 36 years old, who lived at No. 71 Guanxi Pavilion in the city and worked as a dock laborer, was sound asleep at 10:30 PM the night before last. For some unknown secret reason, he had a feud with Chen Youxing, a Shaoxing native (37 years old, also a laborer) who lived with him. Seeing Wu asleep, Chen took a kitchen knife and slashed Wu Dongsheng's head and right arm twice, then fled, abandoning the knife. Wu fell bleeding. After neighbors discovered the incident, they urgently called Li Gengchen of the 21st Precinct, who arrested Chen Youxing. Wu Dongsheng was found barely alive and unable to speak. He was immediately hired a car and sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of his injuries, there were concerns about his life. Chen Youxing was handed over to the precinct. After questioning by Chief Liu, Chen Youxing confessed that he had no feud with Wu Dongsheng and that he was instigated to commit the crime by Lu Quansheng, a native of Ningbo, who lived at No. 47 Guanyin Pavilion. Chief Liu then arrested Lu Quansheng. After questioning, Lu Quansheng denied the allegations, claiming that Chen Youxing was trying to implicate him because Chen Youxing had been slapped by Lu. Subsequently, Lu Quansheng's uncle, Fu Amao, went to the precinct to testify, proving that Chen Youxing was falsely implicating Lu Quansheng due to a feud. However, the cause of the initial conflict and the true facts remained unclear, making the case confusing. As the case involved injury, all the witnesses and the murder weapon were sent to the District Court for legal proceedings.

Murder Case at the Zhabei Theater: Caused by the Installation of a Poison Device, the Murderer Didn't Escape After the Axeing 155

Yesterday at 3:30 PM, while the audience was absorbed in the performance at the Zhabei Theater at the intersection of Datong Road and Mongolia Road in Zhabei, a spectator in the third seat of the fourth row on the ground floor was suddenly struck twice on the head with a woodcutter's axe by someone behind him. The injured person immediately fell to the ground, bleeding profusely. The audience stood up in alarm, and the timid ran out, causing chaos. The performance was immediately stopped. When the theater staff arrived and inquired, the murderer was still standing beside him with the axe and did not flee. The theater staff immediately seized the axe and called Zhang Qingjie, a policeman from the 7th Post of the 4th District Public Security Bureau, who took the murderer and the axe to the district. The injured person was hired a car by theater staff member Li Chongshan and sent to Baolong Hospital on Baker Road in the concession for treatment. After arriving at the district, the murderer claimed to be Ni Heshang, 26 years old, a native of Changzhou, who lived in the kitchen shed at No. 18 Faxiang Lane, Datong Road. The injured person was Lu Gensheng, a native of Nanxiang, around 20 years old. One month ago, he and Lu rented the kitchen shed at No. 18 Faxiang Lane to set up a device for selling red pills. Due to poor security, they were arrested by the Public Security Bureau's detective team, but Lu escaped. Later, the Public Security Bureau released me after I was imprisoned for six days, because I was not the main culprit. Because I didn't have money to do business, I borrowed ten yuan at a high interest rate. Today, because the rent was due, I not only pawned my pawn (and showed the pawn ticket) for one yuan and six angles to pay the interest, but he also moved away the utensils and my clothes in the house. This person is very fierce, and I can't deal with him. If I don't kill him, I will surely die in his hands in the future. After investigating, it was found that the kitchen shed at No. 18 Faxiang Lane not only sold red pills, but also provided people for smoking opium. The interrogating officer ordered that the suspect and the weapon be sent to the Zhabei Judicial Branch of the Public Security Bureau for handling, and that an investigation be conducted to determine whether the injured Lu Gensheng was in danger of losing his life. Later, Baolong Hospital reported that the injured man's skull was shattered, and there were fears that his life could not be saved.

How Can a Woman Marry Two Men? Miss Yu Si from Jiangbei Comes to Shanghai to Remarry; Her Original Husband Finds Her and She is Found Guilty 156

Yu Si, a woman from Bentuo Town, Dongtai, Jiangbei, was betrothed by her parents to Miao Zhu from the same town when she was six years old. At that time, she became a child bride. Ten years passed, and Yu's parents passed away one after another, while Miao and others had also grown up. Miao, now 28 years old, worked as a farmer, while Yu was 18 years old. They held a wedding in their hometown on the 18th day of the fifth month of the lunar calendar last year. The couple's relationship was initially very harmonious, but recently, Yu, because she disliked her husband's poverty and was incited by her brother, Yu Shanqing, harbored ulterior motives. On the 3rd day of the second month of the lunar calendar this year, Yu's grandmother passed away due to illness. Miao's father sent Yu Si back to her mother's home. Yu never returned and disappeared without a trace. Although Miao searched nearby, he found nothing and had to ask people everywhere to inquire, hoping to get her back. Little did he know that Yu had already harbored wicked intentions. On the 18th day of the third month, she and her brother conspired with Wang Rusong, a fellow villager, to come to Shanghai by boat to marry Chen Lanpu, a man from Jiangbei. Chen was 27 years old and ran a bicycle rental shop at No. 414 Qipu Road. He had not yet married. Because he knew Wang Rusong, Wang acted as a matchmaker for Yu Si, falsely claiming that she was not yet engaged. At that time, it was agreed that the betrothal gift would be 120 yuan, with 80 yuan paid in advance. Chen, unaware that the woman was already married, chose an auspicious day, the 25th day of the second month, to formally marry her at the Dali Restaurant on Tiantong Road, and they lived together in the shop on Qipu Road. However, less than ten days later, the matter was discovered by her original husband, Miao Zhuqing, who tracked her down to Shanghai. At 3 PM yesterday, he went directly to Chen's house on Qipu Road and found his runaway wife, intending to take her back. However, Yu Si denied that Miao was her husband, claiming not to know him. At the same time, the matchmaker, Wang Rusong, happened to be at the scene, leading to a conflict. It was discovered by a Chinese constable from the 19th Precinct, who took both parties to the Huizi Police Station. After learning the details, Chinese detective Zhuge Huan ordered Yu and Wang Rusong to be detained separately. This morning, they were sent to the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer, Gan Jingxian, stated the above situation, saying that Yu was being prosecuted for bigamy under Article 254 of the Criminal Law, and Wang was being prosecuted for assisting in bigamy. He requested a judgment in accordance with the law. Subsequently, Miao Zhuqing filed a case, stating that Yu was his wife and had secretly fled in February this year. He had only just found her yesterday and requested to take her back, presenting a red wedding invitation. Yu was questioned and admitted everything, declaring that she did not want to go home with Miao. Wang Rusong's testimony was cunning, claiming that he did not know Yu Si already had a husband. The police lawyer, Gan, stated that this matter was entirely conspired by Wang Rusong and Yu's brother, Yu Shanqing, and should be severely punished according to the law. Judge Liu Yugui ruled in court that Miao Yu Si was guilty of bigamy and sentenced her to six months of imprisonment. Wang Rusong was guilty of assisting in bigamy and sentenced him to six months of imprisonment. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be deducted from the imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day.

Publication of the Song Dynasty Qishasha Edition of the Great Buddhist Canon 157

The reprinting of the Song Dynasty Qishasha Edition of the Great Buddhist Canon, which had previously suffered a major disaster, is now underway. The first batch of 50 volumes of scriptures has been published, consisting of a total of 329 works, 616 scrolls, which were engraved during the Duanping, Jiaxi, and Chunyou periods. In the cultural history of our country, and in the version studies of the Buddhist canon, due to economic constraints, only 500 copies were printed. There are many domestic and foreign orders, and it seems that supply cannot meet demand.

Completion of the Qiu Jiang Pier Limited to Three Years 158

Central News Agency reports: In order to promote the construction of Greater Shanghai and prosper the new urban area, the Shanghai Municipal Government plans to develop the Qiu Jiang Pier. All surveying work has been completed, and the Municipal Central District Construction Committee has resolved to complete all construction within three years. The land was purchased by the Central Bank and will be discussed with the Municipal Government for construction. The details are recorded below.

Qiu Jiang Pier to be Completed in Three Years, planned to be built at the mouth of Qiu Jiang in Yinhang District, has been planned for a long time and has already been surveyed. Since the Municipal Government moved to the central district, the Municipal Government has become more active in the construction of this pier. The Municipal Central District Construction Committee has resolved to complete it within three years. The Municipal Government previously intended to invite merchants to contract the project, although some respondents went to negotiate, but no agreement was reached. According to reporter investigations, the Central Bank intends to invest in the construction, but has not yet contacted the Municipal Government, so whether it can become a reality is still unknown.

Central Bank Purchases Land The land was originally private property, with a company named China Enterprise Company occupying more than 800 acres. The Municipal Government, in order to build the pier, had to requisition private land. To avoid disputes, it announced that the land could not be transferred. However, fearing that disputes would arise during requisition in the future, it agreed with the Central Bank to purchase the land. According to the Central Bank, the land price has been paid in full, and it will apply to the Municipal Government for a business license soon for the transfer. The land now belongs to the Central Bank. The Municipal Government has ordered the Land, Public Works, and Construction Bureaus to contact the Central Bank on matters related to the construction of the Qiu Jiang Pier.

Completion of the Central District Telephone Exchange Expected by the End of September: Expensive Telephone Rates in Pudong, Users Oppose Again; All Cross-Border Machines to be Completely Removed This Year 160

Since the establishment of the Pudong Branch of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, telephone rates have been higher than in other districts due to the river-crossing lines. Local residents are dissatisfied with this. All cross-border telephones in the concession area will be completely removed this year. The reconstruction of the Longhua exchange is expected to be completed by mid-May. The Central District Exchange is expected to be completed in September. Details are recorded below.

Opposition Rises Again Since the Shanghai Telephone Bureau established the Pudong Branch at the end of November last year, the prices set for telephones have been more expensive than in other districts, such as the north and south cities, Wusong, Zhenru, Longhua, Jiangwan, because of river-crossing water lines. (The monthly fee for residents in the north and south districts is 7 yuan, and 10 yuan for shops, while the monthly fee for residents in Pudong is 12 yuan, and 15 yuan for shops.) Lei Shi had been opposed by all circles in the area. The Telephone Bureau had requested instructions from the Ministry of Communications, and the result was that it still charged according to the fixed price because of the water lines. Unexpectedly, the Pudong Fellow Villagers Association also opposed it recently because of the high price. It is now known that the Telephone Bureau is still waiting for the Ministry of Communications to handle the matter.

Removal of Cross-Border Machines As for the telephones of the Concession Telephone Company that cross the border and are installed in the districts of Nanshi, Zhabei, Huxi, Dianru, Wusong, Longhua, Jiangwan, and Pudong, the total number is 288. Except for the 78 machines in Pudong District, which were removed in February after the establishment of the branch, the Telephone Bureau has removed more than 30 machines based on the temporary contract. At that time, because the Telephone Bureau canceled the five-cent call fee, the No. 0 manual station connected to the concession was suddenly busy. Fearing that the removal would cause obstacles to telephone services, it was planned to expand the No. 0 station before removal. It is now known that the manual station equipment will begin to be expanded in May, and all cross-border machines will be removed one after another this year.

New Machines in Longhua There were originally more than 80 exchange machines in Longhua. Because the city is becoming increasingly prosperous and the original machines are old and insufficient, the Ministry of Communications ordered 150 of the most modern automatic telephone machines. Since the dismantling and installation began last month, the assembly project has been largely completed. However, due to the continuous rain in the past few days, the outdoor lines could not be installed. Yesterday, Yu Bingjian, Chief Engineer of the Telephone Bureau, told reporters from Xin Sheng News Agency that all projects can be completed on May 10. After the line is tested, the official call period must be extended to around May 20.

Central District After the Municipal Government moved to the central district on New Year's Day in order to plan for the prosperity of Greater Shanghai, the Ministry of Communications believed that prosperity in the city was most important. Therefore, it had purchased five acres of land in the urban area to build a branch. At that time, due to procedural relations, it could not be established early. Therefore, all telephones in the central district are transferred from Zhabei. Dong Ruihua Architects have won the bid to build the branch and have started filling the soil. In order to establish the branch as soon as possible, the Telephone Bureau has limited the completion date to the end of September.

The Chinese Benevolent Children's Association held its 63rd Executive Committee meeting at the Bankers' Association a few days ago. Those present included Kong Xiangxi, Luo Yunyan, Fei Meide, Lin Kanghou, Sun Ruihuang, Ying Shi, Le Lingsheng, Zhao Jinqing, Fei Wusheng, Hu Mengjia, Wu Weide, Li Ting'an, Wang Xiaolai, Xu Jianping, Wang Guanyi, and over twenty others. Unfortunately, heaven did not grant her a long life, and she passed away suddenly, and her colleagues mourned her greatly. To fulfill her unfinished benevolent will and to commemorate her past contributions, it was proposed to raise $6,000 to build a memorial hall at the Jiangwan Yeyuan Children's Sanatorium to cherish her memory forever. Everyone unanimously approved the proposal and resolved that the association would advance $6,000 to start construction before the funds were raised and that construction would proceed immediately. It is reported that the architectural style of this hall will be Chinese with scientific equipment. If the construction cost exceeds $6,000, additional funds will be sought. The sanatorium will have both medical and educational departments so that impoverished children suffering from lung disease, tuberculosis, and rickets will not only receive medical treatment during their convalescence but also enjoy educational activities. At the same time, the sanatorium is located in the southernmost part of Yeyuan, facing the water and nestled against the mountains, with a superior environment where convalescing children can enjoy beautiful scenery, experience pleasant sensations, promote health, and benefit from education. This is a groundbreaking endeavor in the field of children's welfare and an outstanding memorial hall.

Emergency Joint Meeting of Silk and Electrical Machinery Industry Associations Yesterday Regarding the Detention of Domestic Silk Products in Guangzhou 165

The Shanghai Silk Industry Association learned that domestic intertwined silk products shipped from Shanghai to Guangdong by Guangdong Zhongxing Company were detained and classified as foreign goods requiring special taxes. Despite the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce providing additional proof, the goods were still not released, and over 3,000 bolts of silk were detained. As a result, Guangdong merchants have been sending telegrams to halt the shipment of domestic silk, causing great panic. Therefore, yesterday, the association, together with the Electrical Machinery and Silk Weaving Factory Association, held an emergency joint meeting, inviting representatives from the Guangdong Silk and Cloth Industry Association to attend and discuss solutions. Over twenty people attended, including Lou Fengshao, Tu Shenying, Zhang Hongsun, Lu Zhengbing, Cao Zhixiang, Wu Xingcha, Shao Maozhang, Wu Zhihao, Pan Runsheng, Shen Ji'en, Xi Gongshi, Gao Shiheng, Qian Jixi, Wu Qinxuan, Zhu Yiliang, Chen Yusheng, Deng Hanchen, Lu Shunchou, Lei Songpan, and Chen Depei. Lu Zhengbing served as chairman, and Li Boheng recorded the minutes. After the chairman reported on the detention of goods in Guangzhou, all agreed that the Guangdong Zhongxing Company was established to collect special taxes on foreign cloth and that the domestic silk products, manufactured in domestic factories and conforming to the fourth-class domestic product standard promulgated by the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce, were completely unrelated. However, the company forced the issue and deliberately made things difficult. If they did not fight hard, the day of factory closures and business shutdowns would be imminent. It was resolved to send a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce requesting them to send telegrams to the Central Party, government departments, the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, and the Guangdong Provincial Finance Department, asking them to order Zhongxing Company to release all the detained domestic silk products as soon as possible to maintain the domestic silk business. Pan Runsheng and Lou Fengshao from the silk industry, Gao Shiheng and Qian Boxi from the electrical machinery industry, and Chen Yusheng, Deng Hanchen, and Chen Weihan from the Guangdong silk and cloth industry were immediately appointed as representatives to bring petitions to Beijing and Guangdong, vowing to fight for their rights. It is reported that the representatives are scheduled to depart tomorrow, first going to the capital.

Reinstatement of Special Tax on Pisi 166

The Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance sent a letter to the Shanghai Pisi Tobacco Industry Association, document number Shui Zi 196, on the 13th of this month, stating: "We hereby inform you that after the Fujian Incident occurred in November of last year, all native tobacco leaves and their processed tobacco silk from that province, transported into the special tax zone of the six provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, were subject to the regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Finance. These regulations stipulated that the first special tax authority at the point of entry should collect the special tax, issue a tax payment certificate, and affix a stamp to the packages before they could be transported to Shanghai. This department has previously informed your association of these regulations. Now that the Fujian Rebellion has been quelled, the Fujian Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau has reported that it has taken over the local areas of the province, except for the Ting and Long prefectures, where banditry has not subsided. The bureau has dispatched personnel to take over the various sub-bureaus and supervise the implementation of the native tobacco special tax. The Ministry of Finance has approved that since the various prefectures in the province have resumed the special tax system, all native tobacco leaves and tobacco silk from that province that have paid the special tax should be allowed to pass through the special tax zone of each province upon presentation of the tax payment certificate or shipping permit, with a stamp affixed to the package, after inspection by the relevant special tax authority. This will restore the original situation and benefit commercial transportation. As for the Ting and Long prefectures, where banditry has not subsided and the bureau has not yet dispatched personnel to take over, the method of supplementary tax payment should be restored when native tobacco leaves and tobacco silk from these two prefectures are transported into the special tax zone to maintain tax administration. In October of last year, your association stated that the tobacco silk produced in the Yongding area of Ting prefecture, transported from Shantou to Shanghai, and shipped by post from the place of origin or Guangdong province into the special tax zone, was first subject to a tobacco silk tax of 2 yuan per package (equivalent to 100 small packages weighing 67 market catties net) by local authorities in the Yongding area, such as the Post-War Relief Branch and the 7th District Tobacco and Alcohol Inspection Branch and its subordinate agencies (after deducting additional taxes and surcharges). The native tobacco leaf special tax was not fully paid. Later, when requesting supplementary payment of the special tax, it was calculated at 4 yuan 1 jiao 5 fen per 100 market catties. As for the original tobacco silk tax, it was requested that the evidence be verified and the refund be approved. This tax refund should be used to offset the special tax due, limited to 2 yuan per 67 market catties. If there is no such evidence, the full 4 yuan 1 jiao 5 fen per 100 market catties should be collected in accordance with the regulations. Four measures were drafted and submitted to the Jiangsu Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau for review and transfer. This department temporarily approved the implementation of these measures and ordered compliance. Before the Ting and Long prefectures are taken over for special taxes, all native tobacco leaves and tobacco silk from these two prefectures transported into the special tax zone may temporarily be subject to supplementary special tax collection by the relevant special tax authority in accordance with the above measures. Tax payments already made at the place of origin are also allowed to be offset against the special tax upon verification of the original tax certificate, limited to 2 yuan per 67 market catties. However, tax certificates issued by pseudo-agencies during the Fujian Incident shall not be valid for offsetting. The special tax offsetting situation should be clearly noted on the back of each copy of the tax payment certificate by the issuing agency, and the original tax certificate should be attached to the tax payment certificate for verification and submitted together in accordance with the prescribed procedures to ensure accuracy. All of the above should be complied with. This letter is hereby issued for your information, and it is hoped that it will be relayed to all members of the association. In the future, when encountering Fujian tobacco silk being transported to Shanghai, except for tobacco silk produced in the Ting and Long prefectures and transported from Shantou or by post to Shanghai, the previous method of supplementary tax payment and tax refund should be applied. For tobacco silk transported from the special tax zone of the province, merchants should fill out an application form, together with the original and duplicate copies of the yellow declaration form, and submit them to the department for verification. The original yellow declaration form will be endorsed with a stamp and returned to the merchant, who can then declare and release the goods. To the Shanghai Pisi Tobacco Industry Association, Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance, April 13."

Recent Conditions of Japanese Trade with China: Stagnant in Mainland China, Thriving in Eastern Provinces and Dalian 167

According to the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau, the recent status of trade between Yokohama and China is as follows: (1) In January of this year, the port of Yokohama exported 35 kinds of goods to mainland China, the three eastern provinces, and Dalian, valued at 4,900,145 Japanese yen. The statistics for goods exported to the three regions are as follows: Exports to mainland China were valued at 648,263 Japanese yen, with electric wires, machinery, and iron being the main commodities, followed by refined sugar and other miscellaneous goods. The three items of electric wires, machinery, and iron were valued at 102,291 Japanese yen, accounting for one-sixth of the total export value. Exports to the three eastern provinces were valued at 318,292 Japanese yen, with wheat flour being the main commodity, followed by machinery and iron. Wheat flour was valued at 109,573 Japanese yen, accounting for one-third of the total export value. Exports to Dalian consisted mainly of wheat flour, copper, iron, electrical machinery, and refined sugar, totaling 3,933,590 Japanese yen. Wheat flour was valued at 1,131,408 Japanese yen, accounting for one-third of the total export value. Comparing the total value of exports to the three regions, Dalian accounted for nine-tenths of the total export value. (2) A total of 35 kinds of goods were imported from mainland China, the three eastern provinces, and Dalian to Yokohama, valued at 5,508,649 Japanese yen. The statistics for goods imported from the three regions are as follows: Imports from mainland China consisted mainly of cotton, cowhide, and tin, followed by coal, hemp, and other miscellaneous goods, totaling 2,006,152 Japanese yen. Cotton was valued at 684,444 Japanese yen, accounting for three-tenths of the total export value. Imports from the three eastern provinces consisted mainly of soybean cake, iron, and coal, followed by small beans, sesame, and other miscellaneous goods, totaling 3,325,426 Japanese yen. Soybean was valued at 997,584 Japanese yen, accounting for one-third of the total export value. Imports from Dalian mainly consisted of crude salt, followed by old iron, valued at 177,071 Japanese yen. Crude salt was valued at 45,773 Japanese yen, accounting for one-third of the total export value. Comparing the total value of exports from the three regions, the three eastern provinces accounted for the largest share, accounting for six-tenths of the total export value. (3) Trade between Yokohama and mainland China has declined, while trade with the three eastern provinces and Dalian has surged. Due to the deteriorating international relations between China and Japan in recent years, the export of goods to mainland China remains stagnant, and imports from China to Yokohama have not increased significantly. However, trade with the three eastern provinces and Dalian has developed exceptionally well. Most of the purchasing power is controlled by Japanese merchants, and most of the trade in Yokohama is exports to the United States and South America, with only a small amount of trade with Japan. Under the current circumstances, it is expected that trade between Yokohama and mainland China will remain difficult to develop.

According to the Japanese Shanghai Daily News yesterday, the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai received a telegram from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stating that Japan's trade last month showed exports of 175 million yen and imports exceeding 31 million yen. Since January, accumulated imports have exceeded 65 million yen, a decrease of 61% compared to the previous year. Among them, exports to China in March were 9.66 million, while the same period last year had a surplus of 3 million. Since January, the accumulated import surplus has been 2.13 million yen.

The 蒲滙塘 Dike Has Been Built Yesterday 168

The 蒲滙塘 (Pu Hui Tang) in western Shanghai has been neglected for years and is severely silted. Previously, the 94-year-old elder Ma Xiangbo and others initiated a proposal to the War Zone Relief Commission to allocate funds for dredging and building a dike at the Tianyaoqiao Bridge in Xujiahui to permanently block the flow of black water westward. A new channel was dug southward in Xiaozha to connect the Caoghejing River, leading out through Longhua Baibukou and reaching the Xepu River. The entire project was completed last autumn. However, the eastern half of the sixth section (from the eastern end of Zhongshan Bridge, at the pailouwan, eastward to Tianyaoqiao Bridge in Xujiahui) has not been dredged due to lack of funds. The Public Works Bureau has contracted Wang Rongji to carry out the work. Yesterday, he instructed the foreman Liu Renji to supervise the workers in building the dike at the pailouwan. Today, they will begin pumping water, and excavation is expected to begin one week later. It is estimated that the dredging of this section will be completed by the end of next month.

Derailment of China General Omnibus Company Trolley on Route 3 172

Yesterday morning at 8:20 AM, trolley number 40 on route 3 (i.e., the Circular Route) of the China General Omnibus Company, pulling trailer number 73, fully loaded with passengers, was heading north from the Old West Gate towards the Fangbang Bridge and the Yingshi Memorial Tower. Due to the driver's carelessness, the trolley derailed. Since the road was under construction at that location, the trailer also tilted off the tracks. The passengers were startled and quickly disembarked. The China General Omnibus Company trolleys on routes 2 and 4 were blocked and had to turn around at the Old West Gate. The French Omnibus Company trolleys on routes 3, 5, and 6 also had to turn around at Fangbang Bridge. The company was notified and dispatched workers with lifting equipment to lift the derailed trailer back onto the tracks. It took about two hours to move the derailed vehicles for repairs and restore traffic.

The Trial of the Case of Military Officer Li Chao's Wife Accusing His Concubine of Stealing Funds Has Concluded; Li Chao's Condition Has Improved, and It May Be Necessary to Summon Him; Although the Trial Was Concluded Yesterday, the Judgment Has Been Extended 173

Military officer Li Chao, formerly employed at the General Headquarters, possesses a large fortune. In the past, when Li went to Japan, he stored the deeds and account books of his assets in a bank safe deposit box. Li kept the key himself, while the seal required for withdrawing items was entrusted to his beloved concubine, Shi Jingxin. Later, Li returned from Japan and soon fell ill, bedridden and in serious condition. Li's wife, Zhou Likai, fearing that her husband's condition might not improve, urgently obtained the key and opened the box at the bank to inspect the stored items. Unexpectedly, the valuable deeds and account books were missing, and assets worth about 200,000 yuan had vanished. After investigation, it was discovered that the concubine, Shi Jingxin, had secretly taken them away. Zhou immediately sued Shi in the Second Special District Court. The trial concluded that the case should be under the jurisdiction of the First Special District Court. The defendant was released on bail of 50,000 yuan and transferred to the First Special Court. After several hearings, the case was continued yesterday afternoon by Judge Huang. According to lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the Public Concession Police, the plaintiff's husband, Li Chao, has shown signs of improvement, and he requested that the trial be suspended until Li recovers and can personally testify. However, this request seemed legally unfounded and should be reviewed. Judge Huang declared that suspending the trial was legally unfounded and difficult to approve. The facts of the case have been investigated and clarified, and the closing arguments should now proceed. The date of the verdict will be extended. If Li Chao fully recovers before the verdict and it is deemed necessary to summon him, the closing arguments may be reopened. Li and Zhou were questioned again, and then both sides presented their closing arguments. The judge adjourned the court and scheduled a date for the verdict.

Xie Dazhong, an Accomplice in the Kidnapping of Qiu Jianfei, Was Arrested 174

Qiu Guoliang, also known as Jianfei, a local real estate merchant from Qingyuan Lane, Beijing Road, was kidnapped near Guangxi Road and Hankou Road on July 5, 1930, at approximately 1:00 AM. He was held for ransom in a house at 32 Mingde Lane, Huanlong Road, in the French Concession for about two weeks. His family paid a ransom of 40,000 yuan for his release. Later, the police arrested a suspect named Zhu, who was sent to the First Special District Court and sentenced to life imprisonment last July. Recently, Chinese Detective Shen Chongli and Detective Supervisor Bao Shuji of the Hongkou Police learned that an accomplice, Xie Dazhong (also known as Xuedao), from Anhui Province, was hiding at 13 North Zhejiang Road. They coordinated with Western detectives and secretly went to the address, arrested him, and brought him to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the Public Works Bureau stated that the investigation revealed that the defendant was invited by the convicted Zhu to guard the kidnap victim at the location and was paid 450 yuan afterward. He then fled to Fujian, where he served as a police officer. He had only been in Shanghai for four or five days and was arrested by police detectives. He requested an extension to summon the victim to court for identification. The defendant confessed that a friend named Zhu had asked him to go to the location where the kidnap victim was being held and guard the victim with two other people. He did not know how much the family paid for the ransom. Regarding the 450 yuan he received afterward, he stated that he had 300 taels of opium that he brought from his hometown to Shanghai, which Zhu sold for him. He then went to Fujian, where he joined the militia. He returned home when the Fujian Incident occurred and recently came to Shanghai to seek employment. The rest of his testimony was evasive. Judge Xiao Xiefei ordered him to be detained and scheduled another hearing for further investigation.

Zhang Jilan Surrenders and is Detained; Uses False Name to Run School and Forcibly Seizes Land 177

Zhang Jilan, a comprador for the Bank of Taiwan, in the years of the Republic of China 14 and 15, under the pretense of establishing a school, applied to the authorities and was granted permission to seize over 300 acres of farmland in the Yinxiang District of Eastern Shanghai. At the time, he paid a meager official price of two to three hundred yuan, causing thousands of farming households to become destitute and their homes to be reduced to ruins, leading to widespread resentment. The day before yesterday, it was not a scheduled court date, but the lawyer suddenly accompanied Zhang to surrender, and he was subsequently detained. Debate Ends in Gao Xiaochen and Tao Jiaoyao Debt Dispute Case; Stock Inspection is Necessary 178

Gao Xiaochen from Xuzhou, previously represented by lawyer Liu Cailiang, filed a case in the Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court against Tao Jiaoyao from Jiangxi. After the court held two hearings, both times the plaintiff failed to appear in court. The judge, considering the defendant's counterclaim of false accusation, ordered the plaintiff to appear in court in person for further verification. Yesterday was another scheduled hearing, and both parties, each with their legal representatives, arrived at the court to await the trial. Judge Tu Shenjie presided over the trial in the Second Court. First, the plaintiff Gao Xiaochen was questioned regarding his age, origin, residence, and the details of the case. Then, the defendant Tao Jiaoyao was asked if the case could be resolved through amicable relations between the parties. Tao replied that the truth of the matter must be clarified, and he would not be satisfied until the truth was revealed. He claimed that the plaintiff had falsely accused him without reason, and he requested the court to render a fair judgment. At this point, the official debate began. The plaintiff's lawyer, Liu Cailiang, argued that the late Shanghai Police Commissioner Xu Guoliang owed the plaintiff 40,000 yuan. After Xu's death, his family pleaded with the defendant Gao to assume the debt of 20,000 yuan on behalf of Xu and entrusted him to settle the debt. Apart from the 5,000 yuan that had already been paid, the remaining 15,000 yuan was settled by Cao Boshan, who personally handed over two shares of Tongjisheng Salt Company stock worth 15,000 yuan to the plaintiff to offset the debt. At that time, the plaintiff acknowledged the debt and went to the company to verify that there were no errors and canceled the original interest ledger. The plaintiff did not immediately transfer the shares, but shortly afterward, the salt company went bankrupt. When the plaintiff sought repayment from Tao, Tao refused to settle the debt, which clearly constituted fraud. The plaintiff requested that the case be handled in accordance with Article 363, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code, and that a civil suit be filed to recover the debt. The defendant's lawyers, Luo Jiaheng, Wang Zaoshi, and Li Guozhen, argued that although there was a transfer of debt, the defendant had already offset the debt with the shares of Tongjisheng Salt Company. The middleman, Cao Boshan, and the plaintiff went to Tongjisheng together to verify that there were no errors, and the plaintiff acknowledged and accepted the offset. The plaintiff's failure to transfer the shares at the time was his own fault and had nothing to do with the defendant. Furthermore, this debt dispute was entirely a civil matter and could not be considered a criminal matter in any way. The plaintiff should not have rashly filed a criminal lawsuit, which was a deliberate attempt to damage the defendant's reputation and extort money. Therefore, the defendant filed a counterclaim for false accusation, requesting the court to declare the defendant not guilty, reject the civil lawsuit, and punish the plaintiff Gao Xiaochen for falsely accusing the defendant. At this point, the court decided that the stock issue still needed to be investigated, and announced the suspension of the debate. The debate was rescheduled for May 1, and then the court adjourned.

Reading Q&A

Answering Questions—Answering Mr. Xu Lezhen— 189

We have received several letters from Mr. Xu discussing reading problems with us. We have long admired his eagerness to learn and his willingness to ask questions. However, we are especially pleased with this letter because he not only trusts us and reads the books we recommend, but also extracts the difficulties in the books in great detail and discusses them with us. This kind of knowledge-seeking spirit that does not fear trouble and refuses to be careless is truly rare and valuable, and we should respect and emulate it very much. Therefore, even though the books he has read may not be read by all readers, and the nouns and sentences he does not understand may be understood by readers, and seeing this kind of discussion may feel boring, the main purpose of publishing this letter is not to think that these questions should be raised for discussion, but to hope that readers can imitate his spirit of seeking truth, read books carefully, and be able to discuss the difficult parts of the book with us in such a concrete way. If the number of letters like this increases in the future, then we will choose a book that is indeed a good book and a general reading material, and the difficulties raised are more likely to be encountered by general readers, and publish it in the newspaper, because this will also be very beneficial to readers, we think, and its value is probably no less than the reading methods and research and exploration of certain problems published before.

Now we will answer Mr. Xu's questions one by one, but due to space limitations, we can only describe them very briefly; however, if we were answering them separately, it might be more detailed.

(1) I am now starting to talk about the Dialectical Materialism Course, but I don't know what form the book report should take?

Answer: Regarding the reading report, we will put forward detailed opinions in the next issue of reading news, so we will not say it for the time being.

(2) What is the meaning of the two words "reality" and "practice," and how do they differ?

Answer: The "reality" mentioned here has a philosophical meaning, which is opposed to the term "possibility." The so-called "possibility" refers to such a state (correctly speaking, it should be the two words "situation"), that is, the conditions for the existence or occurrence of a certain thing are already met, but we still dare not assert that it will necessarily occur. However, if this "possibility" is realized, then it is "reality." Therefore, the so-called "reality" is a situation after "possibility" progresses to "necessity." As for the word "practice," it has the meaning of "action," which is opposed to and unified with "theory." We can say that "reality" refers to the objective environment, while "practice" refers to our behavior of changing the objective environment.

(3) What is the minority faction? (Page 1 of the original book)

Answer: The meaning of the minority faction here refers to all those who oppose the current socialist construction line in Russia. This term is inherited from the "minority faction" of the majority faction and minority faction in the old Russian Social Democratic Labor Party. The minority faction is also known as the Mensheviks.

(4) What is "Ideology"? (Page 4)

Answer: "Ideology" is the transliteration of the English name "Ideology," usually translated as "consciousness form," and some people translate it as "ideological system." That is, the meaning of "social consciousness" (SocialConscience). The so-called "social consciousness" refers to the emotions, viewpoints, concepts, and ideas of people in a certain society regarding the world and various social phenomena. After these viewpoints are systematized and cast into an entire system of concepts, they are named "Ideology," which includes science, religion, art, and so on. But how does "Ideology" arise? This is because people's consciousness is determined by the relations and conditions of social production. It is a reflection of the existing social conclusions and relations of production, so there is a systematic consciousness in society; therefore, when the conditions of production change, the Ideology also changes accordingly. In class society, Ideology is class-based, and there is no Ideology that is detached from class. The basis for this explanation is: "Objective material existence determines thinking."

(5) "There has been no necessary change in the 'today' problem of socialism." Please explain these two sentences more clearly. (Line 9 on the same page)

Answer: This will be clear after reading the context. The previous article said, "Practice is supported by the conclusions of theory, and it moves forward more certainly." It also said, "Our theoretical thoughts must proceed in the same pace with the practice of socialism." Therefore, the theory should not stagnate and not advance. These two sentences mean that the academic circles (that is, theory) in the Soviet Union in the past have not studied the current problems from practice, but are still following the old saying and distorting it.

(6) What does "starting from objective reality" mean? (Line 3 on page 9)

Answer: This means "to understand the world from practice." (7) What does "to conquer blind necessity" mean? (Line 6 on page 13)

Answer: This sentence is also a continuation of the previous article. Didn't the previous article have these two sentences in the marginal notes? "Not only to explain the world, but must transform the world"; didn't the previous article say... "Revolutionary change objective reality, turn necessity into freedom." Therefore, if you understand the previous article, you will also understand the meaning of this sentence. If you don't understand this sentence, I am afraid that you still don't understand the meaning of "transforming the world." Now I will give you a brief explanation: Capitalism is bound to collapse, but if it is not promoted by human power, it will not be eliminated. Therefore, we should "conquer blind necessity." In other words, transform reality with human power and promote the speedy realization of necessity. (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

Imperial Incense飘渺Green 190

— Princess Der Ling Original, Qin Shouou Translation

Therefore, I couldn't help but worry about the railway workers driving the train. Perhaps some movement of the train might displease the Empress Dowager, and they would be executed along with it. Just a simple word from this old woman, and their heads could be hung up immediately!

At that time, our Empress Dowager was truly like a child who had received a new toy.

Before she boarded this mysterious train, she decided to see what it was like.

After all, what kind of thing was it? So she ordered the palanquin bearers to stop the imperial carriage so that she could command at will. She first instructed the train to move forward slowly. The train moved, and she was truly overjoyed; she even forgot her own dignity, bent down, and stared intently at the spinning iron wheels, while also firing off countless questions. She asked: How is there steam in the locomotive? How is steam made? What is actually pushing these turntables? Why can't the train run on flat ground and must run on rails? Her demeanor completely transformed into that of a child; no one would have thought that she was a tyrannical empress!

The train moved forward and backward according to her commands, forward and backward, until she was satisfied and seemed to understand how the train could move on its own. Only then did she order the boarding.

In front of the carriage she used, there was a wooden board like a gangplank placed on a ship, covered with a yellow velvet carpet. Li Lianying walked ahead of her, holding her arm, and many eunuchs on both sides protected her with their hands to prevent her from falling. As soon as she stepped onto the carriage, the wooden board was immediately removed. (13)

Flagpole 191

— Yanqiao

To eradicate feudal forces, it is necessary to gradually destroy the old feudal remnants. Therefore, the two flagpoles in front of the Jiangsu Governor-General's office in Suzhou could not escape their fate. As for when these two flagpoles were erected, there is no way to verify. Now, the Wuxian County Government, feeling they are useless to keep but a pity to discard, has given them to Soochow University. Soochow University originally intended to move them and use them as flagpoles for the national flag. They first hired workers to estimate the moving project, but those workers shook their heads, because the height of four or five zhang (approximately 13-17 meters) meant they could neither be carried upright nor lifted horizontally. In the end, they had to cut them into three sections and transport them on flatbed carts, abandoning the original plan and using them for other purposes. Everyone has a feeling: how much manpower was spent back then to cut them down from the mountains and transport them into Suzhou city? The power of the feudal era is truly astonishing. Perhaps even houses were demolished when turning corners, who knows.

Flagpoles are not unique to government offices; some temples also have them, and even families with successful candidates in the imperial examinations have them. It is said that after passing the imperial examination, one had to erect a flagpole. The Peng family in Suzhou's Fengmen, with ancestors and descendants who were top scholars and brothers who passed the examination together, was the family with the most successful candidates. Therefore, there was a forest of flagpoles in front of their house. Although the flagpoles are no longer there today, the stone pillars supporting the flagpoles still stand in a row. The people of Suzhou call their home "Qigan Li" (Flagpole Lane), and these kinds of flagpoles are filled with the stench of the imperial examination system.

Speaking of flagpoles, there is also a little anecdote: those old flagpoles that once stood in front of the Governor-General's office raised the new flags of the "Jiangsu Military Governor's Office" and "Revive the Han and Pacify the People" on September 16th of the Xinhai year (1911). So, these two flagpoles can also be considered founding heroes of the Party and the Nation, ha ha!

Wireless Telephone 192

— Weijing

The wireless telephone has now become an indispensable decoration in upscale homes and large stores.

A store equipped with a radio, even in these economically depressed times, can attract a few nominal customers who don't buy anything but just listen to the radio, constantly stationed at the entrance. Although this situation will absolutely not have any positive impact on business, in terms of show, it's still better than the clerks with their hands in their sleeves, leaning on the counter and watching sparrows dance in front of the door. This is the motivation for stores to install wireless telephones.

In families, the old lady who loves to chant Buddha's name can hear Amitabha Buddha on the radio. The young lady who loves to listen to "The Story of Three Smiles" and "The Pearl Pagoda" can hear the clanging tunes of Fang Qing and Tang Bohu on the radio. The young mistress has no other hobbies except for Suzhou opera and Shanghai tunes, so she can light a cigarette and listen to "Eighteen Touches" and "Little Widow." If she tunes in just right, she might even catch "Peach Blossom River" or a lullaby, which can be quite interesting. The eldest, second, and third young ladies bring their sweethearts home on their days off, waiting for jazz music on the radio, hugging and cuddling, getting what they want. This is the reason why upscale families cannot do without wireless telephones. Wireless telephones are all the rage; playing phonographs is outdated. However, radio broadcasts still have many record programs. Although records are out of fashion, they are still very popular in broadcasts, which is a rather interesting phenomenon.

Children 193

— Dinghua

Stepping on the creaking frozen road, facing the whistling, sharp wind, a group of children walked towards a village town in twos and threes. A thin, small carrying pole, with two heavy baskets hanging on each end, rested on everyone's shoulder, and their clothes were full of holes. Before dawn, they had already reached the entrance of the town.

"Malt candy... Old man!" The voice was like a cuckoo in the middle of the night, made even more eerie by the wind.

"Malt candy, old man... Hey, old man..." They walked all over East Street, South Street, West Street, North Street, all the streets in the town. Each person's basket was still full.

"Malt candy, old man... Hey... old man." Hunger and cold raised their voices.

Snap! The upstairs window of a house facing the street opened. Dozens of eyes simultaneously shot a beam of hope upward. "Making a ruckus on the street early in the morning, disturbing my old lady's sleep! You little country bastards, no parents to discipline you!" A mouthful of phlegm, acting as the "accompaniment" to the cursing, fell to the ground.

Snap! The window closed again.

"Want malt candy! Want malt candy!" The voice was much lower.

The children still carried the full baskets of malt candy back, knowing that there would be no food to eat today.

Chapter 27: Resentment Vanishes in the Dark, Compassionate Heart is Touched; Idle Sorrow Arises After Drunkenness, Old Matters are Hard to Forget

He thought that he had no need to avoid her. Therefore, from afar, he took off his fur hat and nodded to Guizhi. How could Guizhi ignore him? So she nodded in return and smiled, "Second Master has come back for the New Year." Ji Zhi smiled, "The Chinese always have such deep family values. If I didn't come back, I couldn't face my elder brother and sister-in-law. Mrs. Zhao has gained weight since I last saw her." These three words, "Mrs. Zhao," were the first time Gan Jizhi had called her that, and it was also the first change in address since they had known each other. For some unknown reason, Guizhi's heart immediately pounded when she heard this form of address, and her face flushed. She forced a smile and replied, "Isn't that right? People just get stupider as they grow older." As she spoke, she pulled the scarf she had added forward, trying to cover her pregnant belly. Ji Zhi put his hat back on and clasped his sleeves together, looking very composed as he walked towards the street. At this time, Guizhi saw him clearly. His complexion was the opposite of what it used to be, very haggard. The dry and disheveled hair was visible outside the fur hat, showing that he no longer had the rich and elegant air he once had. Guizhi thought, "Since he has treated me with such openness, I might as well treat him with the same generosity." So she smiled at him and said, "Second Master Gan has become thinner." Ji Zhi raised his head and sighed deeply, "How could I gain weight? As the saying goes, 'A spacious home produces young masters,' and I am the opposite of those five words. Mrs. Zhao, do you believe that life is full of joys and sorrows, partings and reunions, just like a play? In the end, it's all empty." Guizhi turned her head to look at the house and then said to Ji Zhi, "Second Master Gan, why are you making such complaints?" Ji Zhi said, "I'm not complaining, I'm telling the truth. You see, I'll be a monk soon." Guizhi smiled, "Why are you saying these things during the New Year?" Ji Zhi said, "If it weren't for the New Year, I wouldn't be making these complaints. Think about it, how quickly does time pass?" (364)

Rambling

Research on Inkstones (24) 196

— Wuliao Ke (Bored Guest)

Other Famous Inkstones

The general characteristics of the Duan, She, and Cheng inkstones have been described above. Besides these three, there are a few other extremely famous inkstones that are rarely seen in genuine form today, or could even be said to be non-existent, but they are the objects of dreams for inkstone lovers, so it is also necessary to briefly describe them.

1. Ancient Tile Inkstones and Ancient Bricks

I have not researched ancient tile inkstones very much, because very few ancient tile inkstones have been passed down to the present day. There are also many imitations made in the Tang and Song dynasties, and it is quite difficult to distinguish the genuine from the fake, so it does not arouse my interest in research. Therefore, today I will only briefly discuss what I know. The ancient tile inkstones that I have seen are only the Weiyang, Tongque, Xinghe, and Shiqu varieties. The most famous are the Weiyang and Tongque.

Weiyang Tiles: In the seventh year of Emperor Gao of Han, Xiao He built the Weiyang Palace in Chang'an. The tiles of the palace halls were like half-cylinders, and those covering the eaves had their heads facing outward, with a round face of five inches in diameter and a circumference of slightly more than one chi and six cun (approximately 53 cm). There were four seal characters of six different types: "Han Unifies the World," "Eternal Joy Unending," "Chuxu Weiyang," "Eternal Life Without Limit," "Boundless Longevity," "Eternal Longevity," and "Taiji Weiyang." They were about an inch (approximately 3 cm) thick. Later, those who obtained them removed the body to make inkstones, which are commonly called tile head inkstones. The half-cylinder tiles could also be used to grind ink after slightly flattening their backs. However, their quality was slightly inferior to that of the Tongque, and after being buried in the soil for many years, they were quite thirsty for water. However, since the early Han Dynasty to the present, almost three thousand years, it is difficult to obtain them, so people regard them as treasures. Among the verifiable imitations made later, those from the Ming Dynasty are the best. Tang's Inkstone Treatise records that Wang Gongzai, named Zuo, of Jishui, said: "During the Xuande reign, the old prince of the Ning Mansion in Jiangxi created Han Weiyang Palace tile inkstones, changing them to the current cloth tile style, which were extremely exquisite and were often given to visiting officials as treasures for enjoyment. Grinding ink on them did not make them thirsty for water. There was an inscription on the surface with eleven lines, each line with six characters, and at the end, there were three characters written by Yuexian in ancient clerical script. Below were two small seals with the characters 'Ning Guo.' In the middle of the surface were carved four [characters], making a small ring pattern. The inkstone had a water pool, with eight seal characters on the left: 'Ancient Tile of the Yan Han, Bestowed by Heaven,' and on the right: 'Sons and Grandsons Forever Preserve [It].' Below were twelve small seal characters in four lines: 'For Cherishing the Quality of Pottery, It Is Appropriate to Add the Sealing of Jimo.' On the back, in the middle, were written the six large characters 'Weiyang Palace East Pavilion Tile,' enclosed in a square of one cun. On the left were the four characters 'Great Han Tenth Year,' and on the right were the six characters 'Supervised by Marquis of Zan, Xiao He,' all in clerical script, slightly smaller than the middle ones." These inkstones imitated by the old Prince Shen are already rare today. How much more difficult is it to obtain a genuine tile from the early Han Dynasty, which has been eroded and damaged for many years? The tiles produced later were all crudely made and not worth looking at. Therefore, today, if you want to study tile inkstones, you only need one with a relatively ancient color, finer texture, and more elegant clerical and seal carvings to be considered a treasure, without the need to worry about its authenticity.

First Encounter with Misfortune 202

The Whites' left winger, Merlin, made a diagonal kick, which Xu Heng jumped up to deflect behind. This was the Shanghai team's first encounter with danger after kicking off. Subsequently, Wan Xianghua created a favorable situation, but Chen Zhenxiang kicked the ball into the sky. The enemy counterattacked, and A Qiao received the ball from the right and passed it diagonally to the left. Tao Lewei took the opportunity to shoot, hitting the back of the net. The Shanghai team conceded the first goal.

Good News Comes in Succession 203

Li Ning sent a long ball, and Wan Xianghua advanced quickly, dodging the enemy generals and passing to Li Yichen. Li did not hog the ball and passed it to the right. Chen Jiaqiu did not fail in his mission and kicked the ball into the net off the goalpost, tying the score at 1-1. This goal came only a few minutes after conceding the goal. Five minutes later, Zhong Yongsen penetrated the left flank, and the Shanghai forwards surged forward like a tide. The ball was passed from left to center, and Li Yichen and the enemy fought for it, both falling to the ground at the same time. Chen Hongguang reaped the benefits, making the score 2-1 in the first half.

Peaceful Ending 204

Not long after the start of the second half, Wu Youliang intercepted the enemy's path in the middle and passed the ball to the front. Chen Hongguang dribbled and advanced, taking advantage of the enemy's unpreparedness to pass the ball diagonally to the left. Li Yichen fell to the ground and kicked the ball into the net, giving Shanghai a dominant position of 3-1. Subsequently, the Shanghai team frequently substituted players, and the line became disorganized, repeatedly being pressed by the enemy. Fortunately, goalkeeper Xu Heng was still competent, providing temporary security. Until the last fifteen minutes, the enemy generals redoubled their efforts, and A Qiao scored two goals in a row, resulting in a 3-3 draw.

Participating in the Last Match of the Far Eastern Basketball Preliminary Round

North China Decisively Defeated Hubei Yesterday; North China Performed Skillfully, Hubei Found It Difficult to Cope; 72-35, a One-Sided Situation 208

The result of the final match between North China and Hubei yesterday in the Far Eastern Basketball Preliminary Round was a decisive victory for North China with a score of 72-35. Because the game was one-sided, the situation was never tense. North China team had several clever performances in the first half, but in the second half, both sides sent out reserve forces, greatly reducing the interest. It is difficult to call it a wonderful match. The audience numbered around 2,000, the largest crowd for the preliminary round.

North China Basketball Team (Photo by Qichang)

Polished and Skillful Performance 209

In the first half, North China first sent out Tang Baokun and the other five players from Tianjin, the former Lianghua Five Generals. Their teamwork was very polished, and their skillful short passes were especially appreciated. Li Zhenzhong has improved since his last visit to Shanghai. The speed of the whole team was not very fast, and there were very few long shots. Most of the shots that went in were near the basket. It is feared that they will not have such a relaxed opportunity to compete against Japan and the Philippines. Because Hubei team fundamentally lacked defensive strength, Wang Jianmin was barely able to hold his own, and Yu Jingxiao was especially lax on defense. North China was able to drive straight in. In the second half, both sides sent out reserve forces, and Hubei was even worse. North China's reserve force was originally made up of players from Beiping, so they were able to do whatever they wanted. Finally, Hubei's official lineup was sent out again to end the game.

North China Drove Straight In 210

Zhang Guoxun served as the referee. After the two sides engaged, Hubei's Yu Jingxiao made a long shot from the right corner, scoring successfully. Hubei opened the scoring first. Li Zhenzhong flicked the ball twice under the basket, scoring both times. Yu Jingxiao also scored again, tying the score at 4-4. Zhao Zhenzhong brought the ball in and scored 7 points on his own. After 11-4, North China drove straight in without any hindrance. After 19-6, Liu Xueqi replaced Liu Zhenyuan, but contributed nothing. Liu then re-entered. The result of the first half was 31-11.

Reserves Fully Mobilized 211

In the second half, all the official players from both sides withdrew. The North China team was replaced by Wang Yuzeng and others, while the Hubei team was replaced by Cheng Yuehan and others. Wang Yuzeng was as light as a swallow, cooperating with Mou Zuoyun in and out of the basket, continuing to score points. However, the Hubei players were merely second-rate, so the performance became dull. The score became 51 to 16, with an even greater difference between the two sides. Chen Shengkui and others reappeared on the court, but it could no longer add to the interest. The situation became slightly more moderate, and both sides reluctantly finished the match. Ministry of Education Orders Summer Seminars for Primary School Teachers 219

(Nanjing, 17th dispatch) The Ministry of Education issued an order on the 17th, requiring the education departments of all provinces and cities to hold summer seminars for primary school teachers, and set a deadline of within one month to submit detailed plans for approval.

Zhejiang Education Director Chen Bulei Resigns and Returns Home 220

Zhejiang Education Director Chen Bulei, due to being in poor health and unable to cope with the demanding workload, has submitted his resignation to the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Education. The duties of the Education Director have been handed over to Secretary Qian Jiazhi to act as his replacement. This was previously reported in the newspaper. He may still come to Hangzhou in about ten days.

Remarks by Huang Jianzhong, Director of Higher Education, Ministry of Education

Improving Various Aspects of Higher Education: University Presidents Must Not Hold Concurrent Positions, Degrees Divided into Three Levels, Course Standards Must Be Arranged Before University Entrance Examinations, Geng Funds to Subsidize Education, Establish Various Research Institutes First, and Subsidize Private Universities with 720,000 Yuan Annually. 221

Six or seven reporters from various newspapers and news agencies in Beijing and Shanghai, after gathering at the Ministry of Education at 4:00 PM on the 16th, jointly invited Huang Jianzhong, Director of Higher Education of the Ministry of Education, to discuss university education issues. Director Huang received them, and many important points were discussed. The main points are recorded as follows based on his intentions:

University Presidents Must Not Hold Concurrent Positions 222

According to Huang, the issue of university presidents not holding concurrent positions was once advocated by former Minister Jiang. At that time, Jiang resolutely resigned from his position at Zhejiang University in order to implement this measure. The recent amendment to Article 9 of the University Organization Law passed by the Legislative Yuan, the content of which the Ministry has not yet seen. As for which positions university presidents should not hold concurrently, it is not yet clear at this time. It is feared that the amendments this time will be even stricter than before.

Degree Law to Add a Level 223

As for the Degree Law, the Ministry originally considered setting up two levels, Bachelor's and Doctorate. Now, in order to accurately distinguish the levels of graduates, it has been decided to add a Master's level. Therefore, the Degree Law will be divided into three levels. It is currently being drafted and will soon be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review.

Preparation for University Entrance Examinations Begins 224

Regarding the issue of holding university entrance examinations, scholars have advocated for its implementation recently. After careful consideration, the Ministry has also confirmed that it is necessary to implement. However, the prerequisite for implementing this matter is to define university course standards. University course standards are different from the course standards of primary and secondary schools. Primary and secondary schools have fewer subjects and the level is more uniform, making it easier to compile. Universities focus on researching academic principles, and ordinary levels can only be set in colleges or departments. It is impossible to set standards for each course. Currently, medical colleges have collected textbook materials from schools and plan to establish a medical course standards committee to start work. The second step is to research the course standards of law colleges, and then proceed to research the courses of science, agriculture, and engineering colleges in turn. The medical course standards committee will be established in two months, and the law course standards committee can also be established next semester.

Major Universities Establish Affiliated Research Institutes 225

Recently, a joint meeting of various Geng Fund organizations resolved to use Geng Funds to handle various educational undertakings. The Ministry plans to handle the case of universities establishing affiliated research institutes first. However, there are many universities, and it is difficult to handle them simultaneously. It will start with national universities first. The preparation period for this research institute is expected to be three years. The first step is to investigate the existing equipment of each school, and then request funding to proceed.

Executive Yuan Decides to Subsidize Private Schools 226

Huang finally stated that the Executive Yuan has recently approved the subsidy for private universities, and the annual subsidy has been set at 720,000 yuan. How to allocate these funds will be decided after investigating the current situation of each school. Priority will be given to subsidizing more complete private universities.

Key Points for Improving Zhejiang Education: Report from the Ministry of Education Inspector 227

The Ministry of Education previously sent personnel to inspect education in Zhejiang Province. The results of the inspection have been reported to the Ministry of Education. The opinions on how to improve education in Zhejiang are explored below:

(1) Although the province's jurisdiction is not vast, the affairs of the provincial supervisors are heavy, and the existing staff is insufficient to assign. The number of staff should be appropriately increased based on the situation. In most counties, the county supervisors' inspections are not universal, and some counties do not have full-time supervisors. Orders should be issued to add staff as appropriate.

(2) The local education guidance conferences have achieved significant results. However, the content of discussions at the guidance conferences in a few county school districts is too scattered. Efforts should be made to improve in the future, striving to focus on the study of central issues to achieve practical results.

(3) The education staff set up in each county school district is not effective due to low salaries and varying abilities. Salaries should be increased, personnel should be selected carefully, and performance evaluations should be strictly implemented to increase efficiency. The establishment of education committees in various counties is well-intentioned, but in most counties, their work is too lax. They should be urged to encourage them.

(4) Among the provincial schools, there are still several schools such as the police academy, the autonomous specialized school, the midwifery school, the aquatic products school, the agricultural extension personnel training center, and the pest control personnel training center. The content is uneven and should be proposed by the Education Department at the provincial government meeting, together with the relevant administrative agencies, to discuss and improve them, and to make them subject to the supervision and guidance of the Education Department, so as to unify authority. In particular, aquatic vocational schools and their affiliated institutions should be taken over by the Education Department as soon as possible for direct management.

(5) The amount of provincial education funds is not suitable for actual needs, and the expansion of various education undertakings in the future requires funding. Efforts should be made to raise funds to supplement them.

(6) The provincial education funds have been separated. In the future, the accounting staff of provincial education institutions should be directly assigned by the Education Department to emphasize funding.

(7) The amount of education funds in each county and city is mostly insufficient, except for a very few counties. The management situation is also quite chaotic. The Education Department should consult with the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments to formulate appropriate measures based on the situation of each county. On the one hand, it should designate a reliable source of funds to provide effective protection. On the other hand, it should hold all public officials responsible for the task of reorganization and organize special agencies to strictly supervise the implementation within a limited time.

(8) The methods for free places in each county and city vary, and they do not benefit the advancement of poor students. The Education Department should consider the situation of education funds in various places as soon as possible, order the counties to set up scholarships, and the methods for provincial funds to subsidize outstanding students from poor families in provincial secondary schools and above are not appropriate, and should be revised by the Education Department.

(9) The provincial medical and pharmaceutical specialized school is run practically, but the funding is insufficient. Efforts should be made to increase it appropriately to enrich the research and practice room and scientific medical equipment. The recruitment of full-time teachers, the expansion of the number of pharmacy students, and the improvement of student levels should also be promoted.

(10) There are still many vacancies for government-funded students in Europe and the United States. The Ministry's regulations for studying abroad should be followed, and measures should be taken to select and send qualified students to study in Europe and the United States regularly to cultivate talents. Definite regulations should be made for the submission of research reports during the study period and the obligation to serve in the province after graduation.

(11) The promotion of normal education and vocational education in the province has been handled separately by the Ministry. As for the measures proposed by the Education Department to urge private secondary schools to promote vocational education, they are still necessary in principle. However, the specific implementation measures should be formulated promptly after consulting the actual situation. The measures to promote secondary education for girls are in line with actual needs and are feasible. However, attention should be paid to promoting normal education for women and sericulture, weaving, and textile subjects suitable for women's careers.

(12) Most of the county, city, and joint private secondary schools are not well managed, except for a few that are still worth watching. They should be strictly assessed and rectified.

(13) The salary standards for principals and teachers in secondary schools are commensurate with the local cost of living. However, the minimum standards for teachers in junior secondary schools in county, city, and private secondary schools are too low and should be increased appropriately.

(14) Most of the provincial secondary school buildings are insufficient. When the provincial education funds increase in the future, the Education Department should balance the urgency and repair and construct the buildings of the Provincial Hangzhou Normal School and the Provincial Xianghu Rural Normal School in order.

(15) Most of the teaching equipment in various secondary schools is simple and should be enriched to facilitate teaching. The equipment for labor courses is also lacking, and should be added and expanded at any time.

(16) The curriculum content of general secondary schools is rich, and the teaching spirit is also vigorous. However, in a few schools, the experiment and practice are not very effective, and the teaching language is still in local dialect, which reduces the teaching efficiency. It should be improved immediately.

(17) The training in physical education in primary and secondary schools is not effective, and the physical fitness equipment is mostly insufficient. Measures should be taken to implement them as soon as possible. The necessary equipment should be added in stages according to the recommendations of the National Sports Conference.

(18) The number of primary schools in each county and city is insufficient, especially in remote areas. They should be added as much as possible to promote compulsory education. Private schools should be used as short-term compulsory primary schools to provide relief.

(19) Among the district primary schools in each county and city, many schools have small scales, insufficient student numbers, and facilities that do not meet the requirements. The Education Bureau should plan comprehensively to ensure that neighboring districts are hired to jointly establish complete schools with larger scales and more classes to increase efficiency.

(20) The distribution of activities in each group of primary schools implementing compound and single-grade teaching methods is often inappropriate. The guidance agencies should study and guide them carefully.

(21) The promotion of civil schools has achieved considerable results. However, the cause of civil education halls is still too focused on formal display, and the efficiency of guiding social education has not been fully utilized. Efforts should be made to improve them to achieve good results.

(22) The work of eliminating illiteracy and guiding mass sports has not been effective. Plans should be formulated and implemented to supervise progress.
